U.S. state

This article is about the U.S. state. For other uses, see [California (disambiguation)](/wiki/California_(disambiguation) "California (disambiguation)").

**California** () is a [state](/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state") in the [Western United States](/wiki/Western_United_States "Western United States") that lies on the [Pacific Coast](/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States "West Coast of the United States"). It borders [Oregon](/wiki/Oregon "Oregon") to the north, [Nevada](/wiki/Nevada "Nevada") and [Arizona](/wiki/Arizona "Arizona") to the east, and shares [an international border](/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border "Mexico–United States border") with the [Mexican](/wiki/Mexico "Mexico") state of [Baja California](/wiki/Baja_California "Baja California") to the south. With almost 40 million residents across an area of 163,696 square miles (423,970 km2), it is the [largest state by population](/wiki/List_of_states_and_territories_of_the_United_States_by_population "List of states and territories of the United States by population"), [third-largest state by area](/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area "List of U.S. states and territories by area") and the [largest state economy](/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_GDP "List of U.S. states and territories by GDP").

Prior to [European colonization](/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas "European colonization of the Americas"), California was one of the most culturally and linguistically diverse areas in [pre-Columbian North America](/wiki/Pre-Columbian_North_America "Pre-Columbian North America"). European exploration in the 16th and 17th centuries led to the colonization by the [Spanish Empire](/wiki/Spanish_Empire "Spanish Empire"). The area became a part of Mexico in 1821, as a result of [its successful war for independence](/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence "Mexican War of Independence"). Following the [U.S. conquest of California](/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California"), part of the [Mexican-American War](/wiki/Mexican-American_War "Mexican-American War"), California was [ceded to the United States](/wiki/Mexican_Cession "Mexican Cession") in 1848. The [California gold rush](/wiki/California_gold_rush "California gold rush") started in 1848 and led to social and demographic changes, including the [California genocide](/wiki/California_genocide "California genocide"). It organized itself and was [admitted as the 31st state in 1850](/wiki/California_Statehood_Act "California Statehood Act") as a [free state](/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states"), following the [Compromise of 1850](/wiki/Compromise_of_1850 "Compromise of 1850").

The [Greater Los Angeles](/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles "Greater Los Angeles") and [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area") areas are the nation's second- and fifth-most populous [urban regions](/wiki/Statistical_area_(United_States) "Statistical area (United States)"), with 19 million and 10 million residents respectively.[[11]](#cite_note-13) [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles") is [the state's most populous city](/wiki/List_of_largest_California_cities_by_population "List of largest California cities by population") and [the nation's second-most](/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population "List of United States cities by population"). California's [capital](/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States "List of capitals in the United States") is [Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento,_California "Sacramento, California"). Part of [the Californias](/wiki/The_Californias "The Californias") region of North America, [the state's diverse geography](/wiki/Geography_of_California "Geography of California") ranges from the [Pacific Coast](/wiki/Coastal_California "Coastal California") and metropolitan areas in the west to the [Sierra Nevada](/wiki/Sierra_Nevada "Sierra Nevada") mountains in the east, and from the [redwood](/wiki/Sequoia_sempervirens "Sequoia sempervirens") and [Douglas fir](/wiki/Douglas_fir "Douglas fir") forests in the northwest to the [Mojave Desert](/wiki/Mojave_Desert "Mojave Desert") in the southeast. Two-thirds of the nation's [earthquake](/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_California "List of earthquakes in California") risk lies in California.[[12]](#cite_note-CaliforniaEarthquakesHumanRisk-14) The [Central Valley](/wiki/Central_Valley_(California) "Central Valley (California)"), a [fertile](/wiki/Soil_fertility "Soil fertility") agricultural area, dominates the state's center. The large size of the state results in [climates](/wiki/Climate_of_California "Climate of California") that vary from moist [temperate rainforest](/wiki/Temperate_rainforest "Temperate rainforest") in the north to arid [desert](/wiki/Desert_climate "Desert climate") in the interior, as well as snowy [alpine](/wiki/Alpine_climate "Alpine climate") in the [mountains](/wiki/List_of_mountain_ranges_of_California "List of mountain ranges of California"). [Droughts](/wiki/Droughts_in_California "Droughts in California") and [wildfires](/wiki/List_of_California_wildfires "List of California wildfires") are an ongoing issue,[[13]](#cite_note-Elassar-2022-15) while simultaneously, [atmospheric rivers](/wiki/Atmospheric_river "Atmospheric river") are turning increasingly prevalent and leading to intense flooding events—especially in the winter.

The [economy of California](/wiki/Economy_of_California "Economy of California") is the [largest of any U.S. state](/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_GDP "List of U.S. states and territories by GDP"), with an estimated 2024 [gross state product](/wiki/Gross_state_product "Gross state product") of $4.172 trillion as of Q4 2024.[[14]](#cite_note-GDPByState-16) It is the world's [largest sub-national economy](/wiki/List_of_country_subdivisions_by_GDP_over_200_billion_US_dollars "List of country subdivisions by GDP over 200 billion US dollars") and, if it were an independent country, would be the fourth-largest economy in the world (putting it, as of 2025, behind Germany and ahead of Japan) when [ranked by nominal GDP](/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)").[[15]](#cite_note-:1-17)[[16]](#cite_note-18) [The state's agricultural industry](/wiki/Agriculture_in_California "Agriculture in California") leads the nation in output,[[17]](#cite_note-19)[[18]](#cite_note-20)[[19]](#cite_note-21) fueled by its production of [dairy](/wiki/California_dairy_industry "California dairy industry"), [almonds](/wiki/Almond_cultivation_in_California "Almond cultivation in California"), and [grapes](/wiki/Grape_cultivation_in_California "Grape cultivation in California").[[20]](#cite_note-Jason_Gibson-2012-22) With the busiest port in the country ([Los Angeles](/wiki/Port_of_Los_Angeles "Port of Los Angeles")), California plays a pivotal role in the global supply chain, hauling in about 40% of goods imported to the US.[[21]](#cite_note-Karlamangla-23) Notable contributions to [popular culture](/wiki/Culture_of_California "Culture of California"), ranging from [entertainment](/wiki/Media_in_Los_Angeles "Media in Los Angeles"), [sports](/wiki/Sports_in_California "Sports in California"), [music](/wiki/Music_of_California "Music of California"), and [fashion](/wiki/Fashion "Fashion"), have their origins in California. [Hollywood](/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles") in Los Angeles is the center of the [U.S. film](/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States "Cinema of the United States") industry and one of the oldest and largest film industries in the world; profoundly influencing global entertainment since the 1920s. The San Francisco Bay's [Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley") is the center of the global technology industry.[[22]](#cite_note-BEA-24)

## Etymology

Main articles: [Etymology of California](/wiki/Etymology_of_California "Etymology of California") and [Island of California](/wiki/Island_of_California "Island of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Detail_of_Queen_Califia_in_the_%22California%27s_Name%22_mural_%28Lucile_Lloyd%2C_1937%29_%28cropped%29.gif/250px-Detail_of_Queen_Califia_in_the_%22California%27s_Name%22_mural_%28Lucile_Lloyd%2C_1937%29_%28cropped%29.gif)](/wiki/File:Detail_of_Queen_Califia_in_the_%22California%27s_Name%22_mural_(Lucile_Lloyd,_1937)_(cropped).gif)

The word "California" and its namesake ruler, [Queen Calafia](/wiki/Calafia "Calafia"), originate in the 1510 epic *[Las Sergas de Esplandián](/wiki/Las_Sergas_de_Esplandi%C3%A1n "Las Sergas de Esplandián")*, written by [Garci Rodríguez de Montalvo](/wiki/Garci_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Montalvo "Garci Rodríguez de Montalvo").

The Spaniards gave the name *Las Californias* to the [peninsula of Baja California](/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula "Baja California peninsula") (in modern-day Mexico). As Spanish explorers and settlers moved north and inland, the region known as *California*, or *Las Californias*, grew. Eventually it included lands north of the peninsula, [Alta California](/wiki/Alta_California "Alta California"), part of which became the present-day U.S. state of California.[[23]](#cite_note-25)

A 2017 state legislative document states, "Numerous theories exist as to the origin and meaning of the word 'California,'" and that all anyone knows is the name was added to a map by 1541 "presumably by a Spanish navigator."[[24]](#cite_note-26)[[25]](#cite_note-27)

The name is most likely derived from the mythical island of California in the fictional story of [Queen Calafia](/wiki/Calafia "Calafia"), as recorded in a 1510 work *[The Adventures of Esplandián](/wiki/Las_sergas_de_Esplandi%C3%A1n "Las sergas de Esplandián")* by [Garci Rodríguez de Montalvo](/wiki/Garci_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Montalvo "Garci Rodríguez de Montalvo").[[26]](#cite_note-Gudde-2010-28) Queen Calafia's kingdom was said to be a remote land rich in gold and pearls, inhabited by beautiful dark-skinned women who wore gold armor and lived like [Amazons](/wiki/Amazons "Amazons"), and bred [griffins](/wiki/Griffin "Griffin") for war.[[26]](#cite_note-Gudde-2010-28)[[27]](#cite_note-29)[[28]](#cite_note-30)

Abbreviations of the state's name include [CA, Cal., Cali, Calif., Califas](/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_abbreviations "List of U.S. state abbreviations"), and [US-CA](/wiki/ISO_3166 "ISO 3166").

## History

Further information: [History of California before 1900](/wiki/History_of_California_before_1900 "History of California before 1900")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/California_tribes_%26_languages_at_contact.png/250px-California_tribes_%26_languages_at_contact.png)](/wiki/File:California_tribes_%26_languages_at_contact.png)

A map of [Indigenous Californian](/wiki/Indigenous_Californians "Indigenous Californians") tribes and languages at the time of European contact.

### Indigenous tribes

Main article: [Indigenous peoples of California](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California")

California was one of the most culturally and linguistically diverse areas in [pre-Columbian North America](/wiki/Pre-Columbian_North_America "Pre-Columbian North America").[[29]](#cite_note-31) Historians generally agree that there were at least 300,000 people living in California prior to European colonization.[[30]](#cite_note-32) The [Indigenous peoples of California](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California") included more than [70 distinct ethnic groups](/wiki/Classification_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas#California "Classification of indigenous peoples of the Americas"), inhabiting environments ranging from mountains and deserts to islands and redwood forests.[[31]](#cite_note-33)

Living in these diverse geographic areas, the indigenous peoples developed complex forms of ecosystem management, including [forest gardening](/wiki/Forest_gardening "Forest gardening") to ensure the regular availability of food and [medicinal plants](/wiki/Medicinal_plants "Medicinal plants").[[32]](#cite_note-:17-34)[[33]](#cite_note-Cunningham2010-35) This was a form of [sustainable agriculture](/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture "Sustainable agriculture").[[34]](#cite_note-36) To mitigate destructive large wildfires from ravaging the natural environment, indigenous peoples developed a practice of [controlled burning](/wiki/Controlled_burn "Controlled burn").[[35]](#cite_note-37) This practice was recognized for its benefits by the California government in 2022.[[13]](#cite_note-Elassar-2022-15)

These groups were also diverse in their political organization, with bands, tribes, villages, and, on the resource-rich coasts, large [chiefdoms](/wiki/Chiefdom "Chiefdom"), such as the [Chumash](/wiki/Chumash_people "Chumash people"), [Pomo](/wiki/Pomo_people "Pomo people") and [Salinan](/wiki/Salinan "Salinan"). Trade, intermarriage, craft specialists, and military alliances fostered social and economic relationships between many groups. Although nations would sometimes war, most armed conflicts were between groups of men for [vengeance](/wiki/Revenge "Revenge"). Acquiring territory was not usually the purpose of these small-scale battles.[[36]](#cite_note-38)

Men and women generally had different [roles](/wiki/Gender_role "Gender role") in society. Women were often responsible for weaving, harvesting, processing, and preparing food, while men for hunting and other forms of physical labor. Most societies also had roles for people whom the Spanish referred to as *joyas*,[[37]](#cite_note-39) who they saw as "men who dressed as women".[[38]](#cite_note-:6-40) *Joyas* were responsible for [death](/wiki/Death_rituals "Death rituals"), [burial](/wiki/Burial "Burial"), and [mourning rituals](/wiki/Mourning_rituals "Mourning rituals"), and they performed women's social roles.[[38]](#cite_note-:6-40) Indigenous societies had terms such as [two-spirit](/wiki/Two-spirit "Two-spirit") to refer to them. The Chumash referred to them as *'aqi.[[38]](#cite_note-:6-40)* The early Spanish settlers detested and sought to eliminate them.[[39]](#cite_note-41)

### Spanish period

Main articles: [Province of Las Californias](/wiki/Province_of_Las_Californias "Province of Las Californias") and [Spanish missions in California](/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_California "Spanish missions in California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/The_landing_of_Cabrillo_on_California_%28detail_from_mural_by_Daniel_Sayre_Groesbeck_at_the_Santa_Barbara_County_Courthouse%29.jpg/250px-The_landing_of_Cabrillo_on_California_%28detail_from_mural_by_Daniel_Sayre_Groesbeck_at_the_Santa_Barbara_County_Courthouse%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_landing_of_Cabrillo_on_California_(detail_from_mural_by_Daniel_Sayre_Groesbeck_at_the_Santa_Barbara_County_Courthouse).jpg)

Portuguese explorer [Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo](/wiki/Juan_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Cabrillo "Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo") claiming California for the [Spanish Empire](/wiki/Spanish_Empire "Spanish Empire") in 1542

The first Europeans to explore the [coast of California](/wiki/Coast_of_California "Coast of California") were the members of a [Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_Empire "Spanish Empire") maritime expedition led by Portuguese captain [Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo](/wiki/Juan_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Cabrillo "Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo") in 1542. Cabrillo was commissioned by [Antonio de Mendoza](/wiki/Antonio_de_Mendoza "Antonio de Mendoza"), the [Viceroy of New Spain](/wiki/Viceroy_of_New_Spain "Viceroy of New Spain"), to lead an expedition up the Pacific coast in search of trade opportunities; they entered [San Diego Bay](/wiki/San_Diego_Bay "San Diego Bay") on September 28, 1542, and reached at least as far north as [San Miguel Island](/wiki/San_Miguel_Island "San Miguel Island").[[40]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERolle199820–21-42) Privateer and explorer [Francis Drake](/wiki/Francis_Drake "Francis Drake") explored and claimed an undefined portion of the California coast in 1579, landing north of the future city of [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco "San Francisco"). The first Asians to set foot on what would be the United States occurred in 1587, when [Filipino](/wiki/Overseas_Filipino "Overseas Filipino") sailors arrived in Spanish ships at [Morro Bay](/wiki/Morro_Bay,_California "Morro Bay, California").[[41]](#cite_note-43)[[42]](#cite_note-44) Coincidentally the [descendants of the Muslim](/wiki/Agustin_de_Legaspi "Agustin de Legaspi") Caliph [Hasan ibn Ali](/wiki/Hasan_ibn_Ali "Hasan ibn Ali") in formerly [Islamic Manila](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Maynila#Establishment_by_Sultan_Bolkiah_and_the_Sultanate_of_Brunei_(c._1500) "Kingdom of Maynila") and had converted, then mixed Christianity with Islam, upon Spanish conquest, [transited through California (Named after a fictional embellishment of the Arabic Caliph title)](/wiki/Tondo_Conspiracy#Aftermath "Tondo Conspiracy") on their way to [Guerrero, Mexico](/wiki/Guerrero,_Mexico "Guerrero, Mexico")[[43]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERolle199824-45) where they played a future role in the [wars of independence](/wiki/Philippine_Military_Activities_in_the_Americas "Philippine Military Activities in the Americas"). [Sebastián Vizcaíno](/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Vizca%C3%ADno "Sebastián Vizcaíno") explored and mapped the coast of California in 1602 for [New Spain](/wiki/New_Spain "New Spain"), putting ashore in [Monterey](/wiki/Monterey,_California "Monterey, California").[[44]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERolle199826-46) Despite the on-the-ground explorations of California in the 16th century, Rodríguez's [idea of California as an island](/wiki/Island_of_California "Island of California") persisted. Such depictions appeared on many European maps well into the 18th century.[[45]](#cite_note-47)

The [Portolá expedition](/wiki/Portol%C3%A1_expedition "Portolá expedition") of 1769–70 was a pivotal event in the Spanish colonization of California, resulting in the establishment of numerous missions, [presidios](/wiki/Presidio "Presidio"), and [pueblos](/wiki/Pueblos "Pueblos"). The military and civil contingent of the expedition was led by [Gaspar de Portolá](/wiki/Gaspar_de_Portol%C3%A1 "Gaspar de Portolá"), who traveled over land from [Sonora](/wiki/Sonora "Sonora") into California, while the religious component was headed by [Junípero Serra](/wiki/Jun%C3%ADpero_Serra "Junípero Serra"), who came by sea from [Baja California](/wiki/Baja_California "Baja California"). In 1769, Portolá and Serra established [Mission San Diego de Alcalá](/wiki/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcal%C3%A1 "Mission San Diego de Alcalá") and the [Presidio of San Diego](/wiki/Presidio_of_San_Diego "Presidio of San Diego"), the first religious and military settlements founded by the Spanish in California. By the end of the expedition in 1770, they would establish the [Presidio of Monterey](/wiki/Presidio_of_Monterey "Presidio of Monterey") and [Mission San Carlos Borromeo de Carmelo](/wiki/Mission_San_Carlos_Borromeo_de_Carmelo "Mission San Carlos Borromeo de Carmelo") on Monterey Bay.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Father_Serra_Celebrates_Mass_at_Monterey_by_L%C3%A9on_Trousset.jpg/250px-Father_Serra_Celebrates_Mass_at_Monterey_by_L%C3%A9on_Trousset.jpg)](/wiki/File:Father_Serra_Celebrates_Mass_at_Monterey_by_L%C3%A9on_Trousset.jpg)

[Junípero Serra](/wiki/Jun%C3%ADpero_Serra "Junípero Serra") conducting the first [Mass](/wiki/Mass_in_the_Catholic_Church "Mass in the Catholic Church") in [Monterey Bay](/wiki/Monterey_Bay "Monterey Bay") in 1770

After the Portolà expedition, Spanish [missionaries](/wiki/Missionary "Missionary") led by Father-President Serra set out to establish 21 [Spanish missions of California](/wiki/Spanish_missions_of_California "Spanish missions of California") along [El Camino Real](/wiki/El_Camino_Real_(California) "El Camino Real (California)") ("The Royal Road") and along the California coast, 16 sites of which having been chosen during the Portolá expedition. Numerous major cities in California grew out of missions, including [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco "San Francisco") ([Mission San Francisco de Asís](/wiki/Mission_San_Francisco_de_As%C3%ADs "Mission San Francisco de Asís")), [San Diego](/wiki/San_Diego "San Diego") ([Mission San Diego de Alcalá](/wiki/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcal%C3%A1 "Mission San Diego de Alcalá")), [Ventura](/wiki/Ventura,_California "Ventura, California") ([Mission San Buenaventura](/wiki/Mission_San_Buenaventura "Mission San Buenaventura")), and [Santa Barbara](/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California "Santa Barbara, California") ([Mission Santa Barbara](/wiki/Mission_Santa_Barbara "Mission Santa Barbara")), among others.

[Juan Bautista de Anza](/wiki/Juan_Bautista_de_Anza "Juan Bautista de Anza") led a similarly important expedition throughout California in 1775–76, which would extend deeper into the interior and north of California. The Anza expedition selected numerous sites for missions, presidios, and pueblos, which subsequently would be established by settlers. [Gabriel Moraga](/wiki/Gabriel_Moraga "Gabriel Moraga"), a member of the expedition, would also christen many of California's prominent rivers with their names in 1775–1776, such as the [Sacramento River](/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River") and the [San Joaquin River](/wiki/San_Joaquin_River "San Joaquin River"). After the expedition, Gabriel's son, [José Joaquín Moraga](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_Moraga "José Joaquín Moraga"), would found the pueblo of [San Jose](/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California") in 1777, making it the first civilian-established city in California.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/San_Juan_Capistrano%2C_California_%28c._1806%29.jpg/250px-San_Juan_Capistrano%2C_California_%28c._1806%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:San_Juan_Capistrano,_California_(c._1806).jpg)

The Spanish founded [Mission San Juan Capistrano](/wiki/Mission_San_Juan_Capistrano "Mission San Juan Capistrano") in 1776, the third to be established of [California's missions](/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_California "Spanish missions in California").

During this same period, sailors from the [Russian Empire](/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") explored along the northern coast of California. In 1812, the [Russian-American Company](/wiki/Russian-American_Company "Russian-American Company") established a trading post and small fortification at [Fort Ross](/wiki/Fort_Ross "Fort Ross") on the [North Coast](/wiki/North_Coast_(California) "North Coast (California)").[[46]](#cite_note-Historical_Atlas_of_California-48)[[47]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERolle199851–52-49) Fort Ross was primarily used to supply [Russia's Alaskan colonies](/wiki/Russian_America "Russian America") with food supplies. The settlement did not meet much success, failing to attract settlers or establish long term trade viability, and was abandoned by 1841.

During the [War of Mexican Independence](/wiki/War_of_Mexican_Independence "War of Mexican Independence"), Alta California was largely unaffected and uninvolved in the revolution,[[48]](#cite_note-50) though many [Californios](/wiki/Californio "Californio") supported independence from [Spain](/wiki/Spain "Spain"), which many believed had neglected California and limited its development.[[49]](#cite_note-51) Spain's trade monopoly on California had limited local trade prospects. Following Mexican independence, California ports were freely able to trade with foreign merchants. Governor [Pablo Vicente de Solá](/wiki/Pablo_Vicente_de_Sol%C3%A1 "Pablo Vicente de Solá") presided over the transition from [Spanish colonial rule](/wiki/New_Spain "New Spain") to independent Mexican rule.

### Mexican period

Main articles: [Alta California](/wiki/Alta_California "Alta California") and [Ranchos of California](/wiki/Ranchos_of_California "Ranchos of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/1836_alvarado_flag.webp/250px-1836_alvarado_flag.webp.png)](/wiki/File:1836_alvarado_flag.webp)

The flag used by [Californio](/wiki/Californio "Californio") leader [Juan Bautista Alvarado](/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Alvarado "Juan Bautista Alvarado")'s 1836 [California independence](/wiki/California_independence "California independence") movement

In 1821, the [Mexican War of Independence](/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence "Mexican War of Independence") gave the [Mexican Empire](/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Mexican_Empire "Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire") (which included California) independence from Spain. In 1822, the California's first legislature was formed, known as the [Diputación de Alta California](/wiki/Diputaci%C3%B3n_de_Alta_California "Diputación de Alta California"). The [California mission system](/wiki/Missions_of_California "Missions of California"), which controlled much of the best land in Alta California, was [secularized](/wiki/Secularized "Secularized") by 1834 and became the property of the Mexican government.[[50]](#cite_note-nps-52) The governor granted many square leagues of land to others with political influence. These huge *[ranchos](/wiki/Ranchos_of_California "Ranchos of California")* or cattle ranches emerged as the dominant institutions of Mexican California. The ranchos developed under ownership by [Californios](/wiki/Californio "Californio") (Hispanics native of California) who traded cowhides and tallow with Boston merchants. Beef did not become a commodity until the 1849 [California Gold Rush](/wiki/California_Gold_Rush "California Gold Rush").

From the 1820s, trappers and settlers from the U.S. and Canada began to arrive in Northern California. These new arrivals used the [Siskiyou Trail](/wiki/Siskiyou_Trail "Siskiyou Trail"), [California Trail](/wiki/California_Trail "California Trail"), [Oregon Trail](/wiki/Oregon_Trail "Oregon Trail") and [Old Spanish Trail](/wiki/Old_Spanish_Trail_(trade_route) "Old Spanish Trail (trade route)") to cross the rugged mountains and harsh deserts in and surrounding California. The early government of the newly independent Mexico was highly unstable, and in a reflection of this, from 1831 onwards, California also experienced a series of armed disputes, both internal and with the central Mexican government.[[51]](#cite_note-53) During this tumultuous political period [Juan Bautista Alvarado](/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Alvarado "Juan Bautista Alvarado") was able to secure the governorship during 1836–1842.[[52]](#cite_note-54) The military action which first brought Alvarado to power had momentarily declared California to be an independent state, and had been aided by [Anglo-American](/wiki/Anglo-Americans "Anglo-Americans") residents of California,[[53]](#cite_note-Graham1840-55) including [Isaac Graham](/wiki/Isaac_Graham "Isaac Graham").[[54]](#cite_note-56) In 1840, one hundred of those residents who did not have passports were arrested, leading to the [Graham Affair](/wiki/Isaac_Graham "Isaac Graham"), which was resolved in part with the intercession of [Royal Navy](/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") officials.[[53]](#cite_note-Graham1840-55)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/%22General_Vallejo_Reviewing_His_Troops_in_Sonoma%2C_1846%22.jpg/250px-%22General_Vallejo_Reviewing_His_Troops_in_Sonoma%2C_1846%22.jpg)](/wiki/File:%22General_Vallejo_Reviewing_His_Troops_in_Sonoma,_1846%22.jpg)

General [Mariano G. Vallejo](/wiki/Mariano_Guadalupe_Vallejo "Mariano Guadalupe Vallejo") reviewing his troops in the [Sonoma Plaza](/wiki/Sonoma_Plaza "Sonoma Plaza"), 1846

One of the largest ranchers in California was [John Marsh](/wiki/John_Marsh_(pioneer) "John Marsh (pioneer)"). After failing to obtain justice against squatters on his land from the Mexican courts, he determined that California should become part of the U.S. Marsh conducted a letter-writing campaign espousing the California climate, the soil, and other reasons to settle there, as well as the best route to follow, which became known as "Marsh's route". His letters were read, reread, passed around, and printed in newspapers throughout the country, and started the first wagon trains rolling to California.[[55]](#cite_note-57) After ushering in the period of organized emigration to California, Marsh became involved in a military battle between the much-hated Mexican general, [Manuel Micheltorena](/wiki/Manuel_Micheltorena "Manuel Micheltorena") and the California governor he had replaced, Juan Bautista Alvarado. At the [Battle of Providencia](/wiki/Battle_of_Providencia "Battle of Providencia") near Los Angeles, he convinced each side that they had no reason to be fighting each other. As a result of Marsh's actions, they abandoned the fight, Micheltorena was defeated, and California-born [Pio Pico](/wiki/Pio_Pico "Pio Pico") was returned to the governorship. This paved the way to California's ultimate acquisition by the U.S.[[56]](#cite_note-58)[[57]](#cite_note-59)[[58]](#cite_note-60)[[59]](#cite_note-61)[[60]](#cite_note-62)

### U.S. conquest and the California Republic

Main articles: [Conquest of California](/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California") and [Bear Flag Revolt](/wiki/Bear_Flag_Revolt "Bear Flag Revolt")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Fremont_Raising_the_Bear_Flag_%28engraved%2C_c._1860%29.jpg/250px-Fremont_Raising_the_Bear_Flag_%28engraved%2C_c._1860%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Fremont_Raising_the_Bear_Flag_(engraved,_c._1860).jpg)

The 1846 [Bear Flag Revolt](/wiki/Bear_Flag_Revolt "Bear Flag Revolt") declared the [California Republic](/wiki/California_Republic "California Republic") and prefaced the [American conquest of California](/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California").

In 1846, a group of American settlers in and around [Sonoma](/wiki/Sonoma,_California "Sonoma, California") rebelled against Mexican rule during the [Bear Flag Revolt](/wiki/Bear_Flag_Revolt "Bear Flag Revolt"). Afterward, rebels raised the [Bear Flag](/wiki/Bear_Flag "Bear Flag") (featuring a bear, a star, a red stripe and the words "California Republic") at Sonoma. The Republic's only president was [William B. Ide](/wiki/William_B._Ide "William B. Ide"),[[61]](#cite_note-William_B._Ide_Adobe_SHP-63) who played a pivotal role during the Bear Flag Revolt. This revolt by American settlers served as a prelude to the later American military invasion of California and was closely coordinated with nearby American military commanders.

The California Republic was short-lived;[[62]](#cite_note-64) the same year marked the outbreak of the [Mexican–American War](/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War "Mexican–American War") (1846–1848).[[63]](#cite_note-65)

Commodore [John D. Sloat](/wiki/John_D._Sloat "John D. Sloat") of the [U.S. Navy](/wiki/U.S._Navy "U.S. Navy") sailed into [Monterey Bay](/wiki/Monterey_Bay "Monterey Bay") in 1846 and began the [U.S. military invasion of California](/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California"), with Northern California capitulating in less than a month to the U.S. forces.[[64]](#cite_note-66) In Southern California, Californios continued to resist American forces. Notable military engagements of the conquest include the [Battle of San Pasqual](/wiki/Battle_of_San_Pasqual "Battle of San Pasqual") and the [Battle of Dominguez Rancho](/wiki/Battle_of_Dominguez_Rancho "Battle of Dominguez Rancho") in Southern California, as well as the [Battle of Olómpali](/wiki/Battle_of_Ol%C3%B3mpali "Battle of Olómpali") and the [Battle of Santa Clara](/wiki/Battle_of_Santa_Clara_(1847) "Battle of Santa Clara (1847)") in Northern California. After a series of defensive battles in the south, the [Treaty of Cahuenga](/wiki/Treaty_of_Cahuenga "Treaty of Cahuenga") was signed by the [Californios](/wiki/Californios "Californios") on January 13, 1847, securing a censure and establishing [de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto") American control in California.[[65]](#cite_note-67)

### Early American period

See also: [California gold rush](/wiki/California_gold_rush "California gold rush") and [Interim government of California](/wiki/Interim_government_of_California "Interim government of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Treaty_of_Cahuenga.jpg/250px-Treaty_of_Cahuenga.jpg)](/wiki/File:Treaty_of_Cahuenga.jpg)

The [Treaty of Cahuenga](/wiki/Treaty_of_Cahuenga "Treaty of Cahuenga"), signed in 1847 by Californio [Andrés Pico](/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Pico "Andrés Pico") and American [John C. Frémont](/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont "John C. Frémont"), was a ceasefire that ended the U.S. [conquest of California](/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California").

Following the [Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo](/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo "Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo") (February 2, 1848) that ended the war, the westernmost portion of the annexed Mexican territory of Alta California soon became the American state of California, and the remainder of the old territory was then subdivided into the new American Territories of Arizona, Nevada, [Colorado](/wiki/Colorado "Colorado") and [Utah](/wiki/Utah "Utah"). The even more lightly populated and arid lower region of old Baja California remained as a part of Mexico. In 1846, the total settler population of the western part of the old Alta California had been estimated to be no more than 8,000, plus about 100,000 Native Americans, down from about 300,000 before Hispanic settlement in 1769.[[66]](#cite_note-Osborne2012-68)

In 1848, only one week before the official American annexation of the area, gold was discovered in California, this being an event which was to forever alter both the state's demographics and its finances. Soon afterward, a massive influx of immigration into the area resulted, as prospectors and miners arrived by the thousands. The population burgeoned with U.S. citizens, Europeans, Middle Easterns, Chinese and other immigrants during the great [California gold rush](/wiki/California_gold_rush "California gold rush"). By the time of California's application for statehood in 1850, the settler population of California had multiplied to 100,000. By 1854, more than 300,000 settlers had come.[[67]](#cite_note-69) Between 1847 and 1870, the population of San Francisco increased from 500 to 150,000.[[68]](#cite_note-70)

[California Gold Rush](/wiki/California_Gold_Rush "California Gold Rush")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/California_Clipper_500.jpg/250px-California_Clipper_500.jpg)](/wiki/File:California_Clipper_500.jpg)

An ad to sail to California, c. 1850

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg/250px-SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg)](/wiki/File:SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg)

[San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco "San Francisco") harbor, c. 1850–51

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Mining_on_the_American_River_near_Sacramento%2C_circa_1852.jpg/250px-Mining_on_the_American_River_near_Sacramento%2C_circa_1852.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mining_on_the_American_River_near_Sacramento,_circa_1852.jpg)

Mining near [Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento,_California "Sacramento, California"), c. 1852

The seat of government for California under Spanish and later Mexican rule had been located in [Monterey](/wiki/Monterey,_California "Monterey, California") from 1777 until 1845.[[50]](#cite_note-nps-52) Pio Pico, the last Mexican governor of Alta California, had briefly moved the capital to Los Angeles in 1845. The U.S. [consulate](/wiki/Consulate "Consulate") had also been located in Monterey, under consul [Thomas O. Larkin](/wiki/Thomas_O._Larkin "Thomas O. Larkin").

In 1849, a state Constitutional Convention was first held in Monterey. Among the first tasks of the convention was a decision on a location for the new state capital. The first full legislative sessions were held in San Jose (1850–1851). Subsequent locations included [Vallejo](/wiki/Vallejo,_California "Vallejo, California") (1852–1853), and nearby [Benicia](/wiki/Benicia,_California "Benicia, California") (1853–1854); these locations eventually proved to be inadequate as well. The capital has been located in [Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento,_California "Sacramento, California") since 1854[[69]](#cite_note-Wilson_2006-71) with only a short break in 1862 when legislative sessions were held in San Francisco due to [flooding in Sacramento](/wiki/Great_Flood_of_1862 "Great Flood of 1862"). Once the state's Constitutional Convention had finalized its state constitution, it applied to the U.S. Congress for [admission to statehood](/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union "Admission to the Union"). On September 9, 1850, as part of the [Compromise of 1850](/wiki/Compromise_of_1850 "Compromise of 1850"), California became a [free state](/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") and September 9 a [state holiday](/wiki/California_Admission_Day "California Admission Day").

During the [American Civil War](/wiki/American_Civil_War "American Civil War") (1861–1865), California sent gold shipments eastward to Washington [in support of the Union](/wiki/California_in_the_American_Civil_War "California in the American Civil War").[[70]](#cite_note-72) However, due to the existence of a large contingent of pro-South sympathizers within the state, the state was not able to muster any full military regiments to send eastwards to officially serve in the Union war effort. Still, several smaller military units within the Union army, such as the ["California 100 Company"](/wiki/2nd_Regiment_of_Cavalry,_Massachusetts_Volunteers "2nd Regiment of Cavalry, Massachusetts Volunteers"), were unofficially associated with the state of California due to a majority of their members being from California.

At the time of California's admission into the Union, travel between California and the rest of the continental U.S. had been a time-consuming and dangerous feat. Nineteen years later, and seven years after it was greenlighted by President Lincoln, the [first transcontinental railroad](/wiki/First_transcontinental_railroad "First transcontinental railroad") was completed in 1869. California was then reachable from the eastern States in a week's time.

Much of the state was extremely well suited to fruit cultivation and agriculture in general. Vast expanses of wheat, other cereal crops, vegetable crops, cotton, and nut and fruit trees were grown (including oranges in Southern California), and the foundation was laid for the state's prodigious agricultural production in the Central Valley and elsewhere.

In the nineteenth century, a large number of migrants from China traveled to the state as part of the [Gold Rush](/wiki/Gold_Rush "Gold Rush") or to seek work.[[71]](#cite_note-73) Even though the Chinese proved indispensable in building the transcontinental railroad from California to Utah, perceived job competition with the Chinese led to anti-Chinese riots in the state, and eventually the U.S. ended migration from China partially as a response to pressure from California with the 1882 [Chinese Exclusion Act](/wiki/Chinese_Exclusion_Act "Chinese Exclusion Act").[[72]](#cite_note-74)

#### California genocide

Main article: [California genocide](/wiki/California_genocide "California genocide")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/%22Protecting_The_Settlers%22_Illustration_by_JR_Browne_for_his_work_%22The_Indians_Of_California%22_1864_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-%22Protecting_The_Settlers%22_Illustration_by_JR_Browne_for_his_work_%22The_Indians_Of_California%22_1864_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:%22Protecting_The_Settlers%22_Illustration_by_JR_Browne_for_his_work_%22The_Indians_Of_California%22_1864_(cropped).jpg)

Between 1846 and 1873, U.S. government agents and private settlers perpetrated many massacres against [Indigenous Californians](/wiki/Indigenous_Californians "Indigenous Californians"), known as the [California genocide](/wiki/California_genocide "California genocide"). At least 9,456 were killed with estimates as high as 100,000 deaths.[[73]](#cite_note-Madley-75)

Under earlier Spanish and Mexican rule, California's original native population had precipitously declined, above all, from Eurasian diseases to which the [Indigenous people of California](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California") had not yet developed a natural immunity.[[74]](#cite_note-76) Under its new American administration, California's first governor [Peter Hardeman Burnett](/wiki/Peter_Hardeman_Burnett "Peter Hardeman Burnett") instituted policies that have been described as a state-sanctioned policy of elimination of California's indigenous people.[[75]](#cite_note-:15-77) Burnett announced in 1851 in his Second Annual Message to the Legislature: "That a war of extermination will continue to be waged between the races until the Indian race becomes extinct must be expected. While we cannot anticipate the result with but painful regret, the inevitable destiny of the race is beyond the power and wisdom of man to avert."[[76]](#cite_note-:14-78)

As in other American states, indigenous peoples were forcibly removed from their lands by American [settlers](/wiki/Settler "Settler"), like miners, ranchers, and farmers. Although California had entered the American union as a free state, the "loitering or orphaned Indians", were *[de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* enslaved by their new Anglo-American masters under the 1850 *[Act for the Government and Protection of Indians](/wiki/Act_for_the_Government_and_Protection_of_Indians "Act for the Government and Protection of Indians")*.[[77]](#cite_note-79) One of these *de facto* [slave auctions](/wiki/Slave-auction "Slave-auction") was approved by the [Los Angeles City Council](/wiki/Los_Angeles_City_Council "Los Angeles City Council") and occurred for nearly twenty years.[[78]](#cite_note-:5-80) There were many massacres in which hundreds of indigenous people were killed by settlers for their land.[[79]](#cite_note-Baumgardner_2005_171-81)

Between 1850 and 1860, the California state government paid around 1.5 million dollars (some 250,000 of which was reimbursed by the federal government)[[80]](#cite_note-82) to hire militias with the stated purpose of protecting settlers, however these militias perpetrated numerous massacres of indigenous people.[[79]](#cite_note-Baumgardner_2005_171-81) Indigenous people were also forcibly moved to reservations and rancherias, which were often small and isolated and without enough natural resources or funding from the government to adequately sustain the populations living on them. As a result, [settler colonialism](/wiki/Settler_colonialism "Settler colonialism") was a calamity for indigenous people. Several scholars and Native American activists, including Benjamin Madley and [Ed Castillo](/wiki/Ed_Castillo "Ed Castillo"), have described the actions of the California government [as a genocide](/wiki/California_Genocide "California Genocide"),[[73]](#cite_note-Madley-75) as well as the 40th governor of California [Gavin Newsom](/wiki/Gavin_Newsom "Gavin Newsom").[[81]](#cite_note-83) Benjamin Madley estimates that from 1846 to 1873, between 9,492 and 16,092 indigenous people were killed, including between 1,680 and 3,741 killed by the U.S. Army.[[73]](#cite_note-Madley-75)

### 1900–present

Main article: [History of California (1900–present)](/wiki/History_of_California_(1900%E2%80%93present) "History of California (1900–present)")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look_(cropped).jpg)

View of the destruction from the [1906 San Francisco earthquake](/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake "1906 San Francisco earthquake")

In the 20th century, thousands of Japanese people migrated to California. The state in 1913 passed the [Alien Land Act](/wiki/California_Alien_Land_Law_of_1913 "California Alien Land Law of 1913"), excluding Asian immigrants from owning land.[[82]](#cite_note-84) During World War II, [Japanese Americans in California were interned](/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans "Internment of Japanese Americans") in concentration camps;[[83]](#cite_note-85) in 2020, California apologized.[[84]](#cite_note-86)

Migration to California accelerated during the early 20th century with the completion of transcontinental highways like the [Route 66](/wiki/U.S._Route_66_(California) "U.S. Route 66 (California)"). From 1900 to 1965, the population grew from fewer than one million to the greatest in the Union. In 1940, the [U.S. Census Bureau](/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau "U.S. Census Bureau") reported California's population as 6% Hispanic, 2.4% Asian, and 90% non-Hispanic white.[[85]](#cite_note-87)

To meet the population's needs, engineering feats like the [California](/wiki/California_Aqueduct "California Aqueduct") and [Los Angeles Aqueducts](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Aqueduct "Los Angeles Aqueduct"); the [Oroville](/wiki/Oroville_Dam "Oroville Dam") and [Shasta Dams](/wiki/Shasta_Dam "Shasta Dam"); and the [Bay](/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland_Bay_Bridge "San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge") and [Golden Gate](/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge "Golden Gate Bridge") Bridges were built. The state government adopted the [California Master Plan for Higher Education](/wiki/California_Master_Plan_for_Higher_Education "California Master Plan for Higher Education") in 1960 to develop an efficient system of public education.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Paramount_Pictures_studio_gate%2C_c._1940_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Paramount_Pictures_studio_gate%2C_c._1940_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Paramount_Pictures_studio_gate,_c._1940_(cropped).jpg)

In the early 20th century, [Hollywood studios](/wiki/Major_film_studios "Major film studios"), like [Paramount Pictures](/wiki/Paramount_Pictures "Paramount Pictures"), helped transform [Hollywood](/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles") into the world capital of film and helped solidify [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles") as a global economic hub.

Meanwhile, attracted to the mild Mediterranean climate, cheap land, and the state's variety of geography, filmmakers established the [studio system](/wiki/Studio_system "Studio system") in Hollywood in the 1920s. California manufactured 9% of U.S. armaments produced [during World War II](/wiki/California_during_World_War_II "California during World War II"), ranking third behind [New York](/wiki/New_York_(state) "New York (state)") and [Michigan](/wiki/Michigan "Michigan").[[86]](#cite_note-88) California easily ranked first in production of military ships at drydock facilities in San Diego, Los Angeles, and the San Francisco Bay Area.[[87]](#cite_note-89)[[88]](#cite_note-90)[[89]](#cite_note-91)[[90]](#cite_note-92) Due to the hiring opportunities California offered during the conflict, the population multiplied from the immigration it received due to the work in its war factories, military bases, and training facilities.[[91]](#cite_note-93) After World War II, California's economy expanded due to strong [aerospace](/wiki/Aerospace_manufacturer "Aerospace manufacturer") and [defense](/wiki/Defense_industry "Defense industry") industries,[[92]](#cite_note-BWatkins2012-94) whose size decreased following the end of the [Cold War](/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War").[[92]](#cite_note-BWatkins2012-94)[[93]](#cite_note-95) [Stanford University](/wiki/Stanford_University "Stanford University") began encouraging faculty and graduates to stay instead of leaving the state, and develop a high-tech region, now known as [Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley").[[94]](#cite_note-Markoff-96) As a result of this, California is a world center of the entertainment and music industries, of technology, engineering, and the aerospace industry, and as the U.S. center of agricultural production.[[95]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2003115–116-97) Just before the [Dot Com Bust](/wiki/Dot-com_bubble "Dot-com bubble"), California had the fifth-largest economy in the world.[[96]](#cite_note-98)

In the mid and late twentieth century, race-related incidents occurred. Tensions between police and African Americans, combined with unemployment and poverty in inner cities, led to riots, such as the 1992 [Rodney King riots.](/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_riots "1992 Los Angeles riots")[[97]](#cite_note-99)[[98]](#cite_note-100) California was the hub of the [Black Panther Party](/wiki/Black_Panther_Party "Black Panther Party"), known for arming African Americans to defend against racial injustice.[[99]](#cite_note-101)[[100]](#cite_note-102) Mexican, Filipino, and other migrant farm workers rallied in the state around [Cesar Chavez](/wiki/Cesar_Chavez "Cesar Chavez") for better pay in the 1960s and 70s.[[101]](#cite_note-103)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Cesar_Chavez_and_Brown_Berets_at_peace_rally.jpg/250px-Cesar_Chavez_and_Brown_Berets_at_peace_rally.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cesar_Chavez_and_Brown_Berets_at_peace_rally.jpg)

Civil rights activist [Cesar Chavez](/wiki/Cesar_Chavez "Cesar Chavez"), flanked by [Brown Berets](/wiki/Brown_Berets "Brown Berets"), at a 1971 rally during the [Chicano movement](/wiki/Chicano_movement "Chicano movement")

During the 20th century, two great disasters happened: the [1906 San Francisco earthquake](/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake "1906 San Francisco earthquake") and 1928 [St. Francis Dam](/wiki/St._Francis_Dam "St. Francis Dam") flood remain the deadliest in U.S. history.[[102]](#cite_note-IIIMcNeill2004-104)

Although air pollution has been reduced, health problems associated with pollution continue. Brown haze known as "[smog](/wiki/Smog "Smog")" has been substantially abated after federal and state restrictions on automobile exhaust.[[103]](#cite_note-105)[[104]](#cite_note-106) An [energy crisis in 2001](/wiki/2000%E2%80%932001_California_electricity_crisis "2000–2001 California electricity crisis") led to [rolling blackouts](/wiki/Rolling_blackout "Rolling blackout"), soaring power rates, and the importation of electricity from neighboring states. [Southern California Edison](/wiki/Southern_California_Edison "Southern California Edison") and [Pacific Gas and Electric Company](/wiki/Pacific_Gas_and_Electric_Company "Pacific Gas and Electric Company") came under heavy criticism.[[105]](#cite_note-107)

Housing prices in urban areas continued to increase; a modest home which in the 1960s cost $25,000 would cost half a million dollars or more in urban areas by 2005. More people commuted longer hours to afford a home in more rural areas while earning larger salaries in the urban areas. Speculators bought houses, expecting to make a huge profit in months, then rolling it over by buying more properties. [Mortgage](/wiki/Mortgage "Mortgage") companies were compliant, as people assumed prices would keep rising. The [bubble burst](/wiki/Subprime_mortgage_crisis "Subprime mortgage crisis") in 2007–2008 as prices began to crash. Hundreds of billions in property values vanished and foreclosures soared, as financial institutions and investors were badly hurt.[[106]](#cite_note-108)[[107]](#cite_note-109)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Steve_Jobs_presents_iPhone_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Steve_Jobs_presents_iPhone_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Steve_Jobs_presents_iPhone_(cropped).jpg)

The 2007 launch of the [iPhone](/wiki/IPhone_(1st_generation) "IPhone (1st generation)") by [Apple](/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc.") founder [Steve Jobs](/wiki/Steve_Jobs "Steve Jobs") in [Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley"), the largest [tech hub](/wiki/Technopole "Technopole") in the world

In the 21st century, droughts and frequent wildfires attributed to climate change have occurred.[[108]](#cite_note-110)[[109]](#cite_note-111) From 2011 to 2017, a [persistent drought](/wiki/2011%E2%80%932017_California_drought "2011–2017 California drought") was the worst in its recorded history.[[110]](#cite_note-112) The 2018 wildfire season was the state's deadliest and most destructive.[[111]](#cite_note-113)

One of the first confirmed [COVID-19](/wiki/COVID-19 "COVID-19") cases in the U.S. occurred in California on January 26, 2020.[[112]](#cite_note-Wheeler2-114)[[113]](#cite_note-uk.reuters.com2-115) A [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency#United_States "State of emergency") was declared in the state on March 4, 2020, and remained in effect until Governor [Gavin Newsom](/wiki/Gavin_Newsom "Gavin Newsom") ended it in February 2023.[[114]](#cite_note-116) A mandatory statewide [stay-at-home order](/wiki/Stay-at-home_order "Stay-at-home order") was issued on March 19, 2020, which was ended in January 2021.[[115]](#cite_note-117)

Cultural and [language revitalization](/wiki/Language_revitalization "Language revitalization") efforts among indigenous Californians have progressed among tribes as of 2022.[[116]](#cite_note-118)[[117]](#cite_note-119) Some [land returns](/wiki/Land_Back "Land Back") to indigenous stewardship have occurred.[[118]](#cite_note-120)[[119]](#cite_note-121)[[120]](#cite_note-122) In 2022, the largest [dam removal](/wiki/Dam_removal "Dam removal") and river restoration project in U.S. history was announced for the [Klamath River](/wiki/Klamath_River "Klamath River"), as a win for California tribes.[[121]](#cite_note-123)[[122]](#cite_note-124)

## Geography

Main article: [Geography of California](/wiki/Geography_of_California "Geography of California")

Further information: [Northern California](/wiki/Northern_California "Northern California") and [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/California_Topography_and_Geomorphic.gif/330px-California_Topography_and_Geomorphic.gif)](/wiki/File:California_Topography_and_Geomorphic.gif)

[Topographic map](/wiki/Topographic_map "Topographic map") of California

Covering an area of 163,696 sq mi (423,970 km2), California is the [third-largest state in the U.S.](/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area "List of U.S. states and territories by area") in area, after [Alaska](/wiki/Alaska "Alaska") and [Texas](/wiki/Texas "Texas").[[123]](#cite_note-2000_population_and_housing-125) California is one of the most geographically diverse states in the union and is often geographically bisected into two regions, Southern California, comprising the ten southernmost counties,[[124]](#cite_note-126)[[125]](#cite_note-127) and Northern California, comprising the 48 northernmost counties.[[126]](#cite_note-128)[[127]](#cite_note-129) It is bordered by [Oregon](/wiki/Oregon "Oregon") to the north, [Nevada](/wiki/Nevada "Nevada") to the east and northeast, [Arizona](/wiki/Arizona "Arizona") to the southeast, the [Pacific Ocean](/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") to the west and shares an international border with the [Mexican](/wiki/Mexico "Mexico") state of [Baja California](/wiki/Baja_California "Baja California") to the south (with which it makes up part of [The Californias](/wiki/The_Californias "The Californias") region of North America, alongside [Baja California Sur](/wiki/Baja_California_Sur "Baja California Sur")).

In the middle of the state lies the [California Central Valley](/wiki/California_Central_Valley "California Central Valley"), bounded by the Sierra Nevada in the east, the [coastal mountain ranges](/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Ranges "Pacific Coast Ranges") in the west, the [Cascade Range](/wiki/Cascade_Range "Cascade Range") to the north and by the [Tehachapi Mountains](/wiki/Tehachapi_Mountains "Tehachapi Mountains") in the south. The Central Valley is California's productive agricultural heartland.

Divided in two by the [Sacramento-San Joaquin River Delta](/wiki/Sacramento-San_Joaquin_River_Delta "Sacramento-San Joaquin River Delta"), the northern portion, the [Sacramento Valley](/wiki/Sacramento_Valley "Sacramento Valley") serves as the watershed of the [Sacramento River](/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River"), while the southern portion, the [San Joaquin Valley](/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley "San Joaquin Valley") is the watershed for the [San Joaquin River](/wiki/San_Joaquin_River "San Joaquin River"). Both valleys derive their names from the rivers that flow through them. With dredging, the Sacramento and the San Joaquin Rivers have remained deep enough for several inland cities to be [seaports](/wiki/Seaport "Seaport").

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Big_Sur_June_2008.jpg/250px-Big_Sur_June_2008.jpg)](/wiki/File:Big_Sur_June_2008.jpg)

[Big Sur](/wiki/Big_Sur "Big Sur"), on the [Central Coast](/wiki/Central_Coast_(California) "Central Coast (California)")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/1_yosemite_valley_tunnel_view_2010.JPG/250px-1_yosemite_valley_tunnel_view_2010.JPG)](/wiki/File:1_yosemite_valley_tunnel_view_2010.JPG)

[Yosemite](/wiki/Yosemite "Yosemite"), in the [Sierra Nevada](/wiki/Sierra_Nevada "Sierra Nevada")

The Sacramento-San Joaquin River Delta is a critical water supply hub for the state. Water is diverted from the delta and through an extensive network of [pumps](/wiki/Pump_(Water) "Pump (Water)") and canals that traverse nearly the length of the state, to the Central Valley and the State Water Projects and other needs. Water from the Delta provides drinking water for nearly 23 million people, almost two-thirds of the state's population as well as water for farmers on the west side of the San Joaquin Valley.

[Suisun Bay](/wiki/Suisun_Bay "Suisun Bay") lies at the confluence of the Sacramento and San Joaquin Rivers. The water is drained by the [Carquinez Strait](/wiki/Carquinez_Strait "Carquinez Strait"), which flows into [San Pablo Bay](/wiki/San_Pablo_Bay "San Pablo Bay"), a northern extension of [San Francisco Bay](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay "San Francisco Bay"), which then connects to the [Pacific Ocean](/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") via the [Golden Gate](/wiki/Golden_Gate "Golden Gate") strait.

The [Channel Islands](/wiki/Channel_Islands_of_California "Channel Islands of California") are located off the [Southern coast](/wiki/South_Coast_(California) "South Coast (California)"), while the [Farallon Islands](/wiki/Farallon_Islands "Farallon Islands") lie west of San Francisco.

The Sierra Nevada (Spanish for "snowy range") includes the highest peak in the [contiguous 48 states](/wiki/Contiguous_United_States "Contiguous United States"), [Mount Whitney](/wiki/Mount_Whitney "Mount Whitney"), at 14,505 feet (4,421 m).[[3]](#cite_note-Mount_Whitney-3)[[4]](#cite_note-USGS-4)[[note 1]](#cite_note-NAVD88-5) The range embraces [Yosemite Valley](/wiki/Yosemite_Valley "Yosemite Valley"), famous for its glacially carved domes, and [Sequoia National Park](/wiki/Sequoia_National_Park "Sequoia National Park"), home to the [giant sequoia](/wiki/Sequoiadendron_giganteum "Sequoiadendron giganteum") trees, the largest living organisms on Earth, and the deep freshwater lake, [Lake Tahoe](/wiki/Lake_Tahoe "Lake Tahoe"), the largest lake in the state by volume.

To the east of the Sierra Nevada are [Owens Valley](/wiki/Owens_Valley "Owens Valley") and [Mono Lake](/wiki/Mono_Lake "Mono Lake"), an essential [migratory bird](/wiki/Bird_migration "Bird migration") habitat. In the western part of the state is [Clear Lake](/wiki/Clear_Lake_(California) "Clear Lake (California)"), the largest freshwater lake by area entirely in California. Although Lake Tahoe is larger, it is divided by the California/Nevada border. The Sierra Nevada falls to Arctic temperatures in winter and has several dozen small glaciers, including [Palisade Glacier](/wiki/Palisade_Glacier "Palisade Glacier"), the southernmost glacier in the U.S.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Death_Valley_Mesquite_Flats_Sand_Dunes_2013.jpg/250px-Death_Valley_Mesquite_Flats_Sand_Dunes_2013.jpg)](/wiki/File:Death_Valley_Mesquite_Flats_Sand_Dunes_2013.jpg)

[Death Valley](/wiki/Death_Valley "Death Valley"), in the [Mojave Desert](/wiki/Mojave_Desert "Mojave Desert")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/San-miguel-cuyler-hike_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-San-miguel-cuyler-hike_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:San-miguel-cuyler-hike_(cropped).jpg)

[San Miguel](/wiki/San_Miguel_Island "San Miguel Island"), in the [Channel Islands](/wiki/Channel_Islands_(California) "Channel Islands (California)")

The [Tulare Lake](/wiki/Tulare_Lake "Tulare Lake") was the largest freshwater lake west of the Mississippi River. A remnant of [Pleistocene](/wiki/Pleistocene "Pleistocene")-era [Lake Corcoran](/wiki/Lake_Corcoran "Lake Corcoran"), Tulare Lake dried up by the early 20th century after its tributary rivers were diverted for agricultural irrigation and municipal water uses.[[128]](#cite_note-130)

About 45% of the state's total surface area is covered by forests,[[129]](#cite_note-Forestry_2003-131) and California's diversity of pine species is unmatched by any other state. California contains more forestland than any other state except Alaska. Many of the trees in the [California White Mountains](/wiki/White_Mountains_(California) "White Mountains (California)") are the oldest in the world; an individual [bristlecone pine](/wiki/Bristlecone_pine "Bristlecone pine") is over 5,000 years old.[[130]](#cite_note-Lanner-132)[[131]](#cite_note-oldest-133)

In the south is a large inland salt lake, the [Salton Sea](/wiki/Salton_Sea "Salton Sea"). The south-central desert is called the [Mojave](/wiki/Mojave_Desert "Mojave Desert"); to the northeast of the Mojave lies [Death Valley](/wiki/Death_Valley "Death Valley"), which contains the lowest and hottest place in North America, the [Badwater Basin](/wiki/Badwater_Basin "Badwater Basin") at −279 feet (−85 m).[[5]](#cite_note-NED-7) The horizontal distance from the bottom of Death Valley to the top of Mount Whitney is less than 90 miles (140 km). Indeed, almost all of southeastern California is arid, hot desert, with routine extreme high temperatures during the summer. The southeastern border of California with Arizona is entirely formed by the [Colorado River](/wiki/Colorado_River "Colorado River"), from which the southern part of the state gets about half of its water.

A majority of California's cities are located in either the [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area") or the [Sacramento metropolitan area](/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Sacramento metropolitan area") in [Northern California](/wiki/Northern_California "Northern California"); or the [Los Angeles area](/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area "Los Angeles metropolitan area"), the [Inland Empire](/wiki/Inland_Empire "Inland Empire"), or the [San Diego metropolitan area](/wiki/San_Diego_metropolitan_area "San Diego metropolitan area") in [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California"). The Los Angeles Area, the Bay Area, and the San Diego metropolitan area are among several major metropolitan areas along the California coast.

As part of the [Ring of Fire](/wiki/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire "Pacific Ring of Fire"), California is subject to [tsunamis](/wiki/Tsunami "Tsunami"), [floods](/wiki/Floods_in_California "Floods in California"), [droughts](/wiki/Droughts_in_California "Droughts in California"), [Santa Ana winds](/wiki/Santa_Ana_winds "Santa Ana winds"), [wildfires](/wiki/List_of_California_wildfires "List of California wildfires"), and [landslides](/wiki/Landslide "Landslide") on steep terrain; California also has several [volcanoes](/wiki/Volcano "Volcano"). It has many [earthquakes](/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_California "List of earthquakes in California") due to several faults running through the state, the largest being the [San Andreas Fault](/wiki/San_Andreas_Fault "San Andreas Fault"). About 37,000 [earthquakes](/wiki/Earthquake "Earthquake") are recorded each year; most are too small to be felt.[[132]](#cite_note-134) Among Americans at risk of serious harm from a major earthquake, two-thirds of that population are residents of California.[[12]](#cite_note-CaliforniaEarthquakesHumanRisk-14)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_California.png/330px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_California.png)](/wiki/File:K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_California.png)

[Köppen climate](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") types

### Climate

Main article: [Climate of California](/wiki/Climate_of_California "Climate of California")

Further information: [Climate change in California](/wiki/Climate_change_in_California "Climate change in California")

Most of the state has a [Mediterranean climate](/wiki/Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate"). The cool [California Current](/wiki/California_Current "California Current") offshore often creates summer [fog](/wiki/Fog "Fog") near the coast. Farther inland, there are colder winters and hotter summers. The maritime moderation results in the shoreline summertime temperatures of Los Angeles and [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco "San Francisco") being the coolest of all major metropolitan areas of the U.S. and uniquely cool compared to areas on the same latitude in the interior and on the east coast of the North American continent. Even the [San Diego](/wiki/San_Diego "San Diego") shoreline bordering Mexico is cooler in summer than most areas in the contiguous U.S. Just a few miles inland, summer temperature extremes are significantly higher, with downtown Los Angeles being several degrees [warmer](/wiki/Climate_of_the_Los_Angeles_Basin "Climate of the Los Angeles Basin") than at the coast. The same [microclimate](/wiki/Microclimate "Microclimate") phenomenon is seen in the [climate of the Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area#Climate "San Francisco Bay Area"), where areas sheltered from the ocean experience significantly hotter summers and colder winters in contrast with nearby areas closer to the ocean.[[133]](#cite_note-135)[[134]](#cite_note-136)[[135]](#cite_note-137)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/AERONET_La_Jolla.2007295.terra.250m.jpg/250px-AERONET_La_Jolla.2007295.terra.250m.jpg)](/wiki/File:AERONET_La_Jolla.2007295.terra.250m.jpg)

[California wildfires](/wiki/List_of_California_wildfires "List of California wildfires") affect the state yearly. The [Santa Ana winds](/wiki/Santa_Ana_winds "Santa Ana winds") often expand fires and spread smoke over hundreds of miles.

Northern parts of the state have more rain than the south. California's mountain ranges also influence the climate: some of the rainiest parts of the state are west-facing mountain slopes. Coastal northwestern California has a [temperate climate](/wiki/Temperate_climate "Temperate climate"), and the Central Valley has a Mediterranean climate but with greater temperature extremes than the coast. The high mountains, including the Sierra Nevada, have an [alpine climate](/wiki/Alpine_climate "Alpine climate") with snow in winter and mild to moderate heat in summer.

California's mountains produce [rain shadows](/wiki/Rain_shadow "Rain shadow") on the eastern side, creating extensive [deserts](/wiki/Desert "Desert"). The higher elevation deserts of [eastern California](/wiki/Eastern_California "Eastern California") have hot summers and cold winters, while the low deserts east of the Southern California mountains have hot summers and nearly frostless mild winters. [Death Valley](/wiki/Death_Valley "Death Valley"), a desert with large expanses below sea level, is considered the hottest location in the world; the highest temperature in the world,[[136]](#cite_note-newRecord-138)[[137]](#cite_note-139) 134 °F (56.7 °C), was recorded there on July 10, 1913. The lowest temperature in California was −45 °F (−43 °C) on January 20, 1937, in [Boca](/wiki/Boca,_California "Boca, California").[[138]](#cite_note-140)

The table below lists average temperatures for January and August in a selection of places throughout the state; some highly populated and some not. This includes the relatively cool summers of the [Humboldt Bay](/wiki/Humboldt_Bay "Humboldt Bay") region around [Eureka](/wiki/Eureka,_California "Eureka, California"), the extreme heat of [Death Valley](/wiki/Death_Valley "Death Valley"), and the mountain climate of [Mammoth](/wiki/Mammoth_Lakes,_California "Mammoth Lakes, California") in the Sierra Nevada.

Average temperatures and precipitation for selected communities in California[[139]](#cite_note-California_climate_averages-141)

| Location | August (°F) | August (°C) | January (°F) | January (°C) | Annual precipitation (mm/in) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles") | 83/64 | 29/18 | 66/48 | 20/8 | 377/15 |
| [LAX/LA Beaches](/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport "Los Angeles International Airport") | 75/64 | 23/18 | 65/49 | 18/9 | 326/13 |
| [San Diego](/wiki/San_Diego,_California "San Diego, California") | 76/67 | 24/19 | 65/49 | 18/9 | 262/10 |
| [San Jose](/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California") | 82/58 | 27/14 | 58/42 | 14/5 | 401/16 |
| [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco,_California "San Francisco, California") | 67/54 | 20/12 | 56/46 | 14/8 | 538/21 |
| [Fresno](/wiki/Fresno,_California "Fresno, California") | 97/66 | 34/19 | 55/38 | 12/3 | 292/11 |
| [Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento,_California "Sacramento, California") | 91/58 | 33/14 | 54/39 | 12/3 | 469/18 |
| [Oakland](/wiki/Oakland,_California "Oakland, California") | 73/58 | 23/14 | 58/44 | 14/7 | 588/23 |
| [Bakersfield](/wiki/Bakersfield,_California "Bakersfield, California") | 96/69 | 36/21 | 56/39 | 13/3 | 165/7 |
| [Riverside](/wiki/Riverside,_California "Riverside, California") | 94/60 | 35/18 | 67/39 | 19/4 | 260/10 |
| [Eureka](/wiki/Eureka,_California "Eureka, California") | 62/53 | 16/11 | 54/41 | 12/5 | 960/38 |
| [Death Valley](/wiki/Death_Valley "Death Valley") | 115/86 | 46/30 | 67/40 | 19/4 | 60/2 |
| [Mammoth Lakes](/wiki/Mammoth_Lakes,_California "Mammoth Lakes, California") | 77/45 | 25/7 | 40/15 | 4/ −9 | 583/23 |

The wide range of climates leads to a high demand for water. Over time, [droughts](/wiki/Droughts_in_California "Droughts in California") have been increasing [due to climate change](/wiki/Climate_change_in_California "Climate change in California") and [overextraction](/wiki/Water_extraction "Water extraction"),[[140]](#cite_note-142) becoming less seasonal and more year-round, further straining California's [electricity supply](/wiki/Electricity_supply "Electricity supply")[[141]](#cite_note-143) and [water security](/wiki/Water_security "Water security")[[142]](#cite_note-144)[[143]](#cite_note-145) and having an impact on California business, industry, and agriculture.[[144]](#cite_note-146)

In 2022, a new state program was created in collaboration with [indigenous peoples of California](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California") to revive the practice of [controlled burns](/wiki/Controlled_burn "Controlled burn") as a way of clearing excessive forest debris and making landscapes more resilient to wildfires. [Native American use of fire in ecosystem](/wiki/Native_American_use_of_fire_in_ecosystems "Native American use of fire in ecosystems") management was outlawed in 1911, yet has now been recognized.[[13]](#cite_note-Elassar-2022-15)

### Ecology

Main articles: [Ecology of California](/wiki/Ecology_of_California "Ecology of California") and [Environment of California](/wiki/Environment_of_California "Environment of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Mount_Whitney_2003-03-25.jpg/250px-Mount_Whitney_2003-03-25.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mount_Whitney_2003-03-25.jpg)

[Mount Whitney](/wiki/Mount_Whitney "Mount Whitney"), in the Sierra Nevada, is the highest mountain in the [contiguous U.S.](/wiki/Contiguous_U.S. "Contiguous U.S.")

California is one of the ecologically richest and most diverse parts of the world, and includes some of the most endangered ecological communities. California is part of the [Nearctic realm](/wiki/Nearctic_realm "Nearctic realm") and spans a number of terrestrial [ecoregions](/wiki/Ecoregion "Ecoregion").[[145]](#cite_note-The_California_Invasive_Species_List-147)

California's large number of [endemic](/wiki/Endemic_(ecology) "Endemic (ecology)") species includes [relict](/wiki/Relict_(biology) "Relict (biology)") species, which have died out elsewhere, such as the Catalina ironwood (*[Lyonothamnus floribundus](/wiki/Lyonothamnus_floribundus "Lyonothamnus floribundus")*). Many other endemics originated through differentiation or [adaptive radiation](/wiki/Adaptive_radiation "Adaptive radiation"), whereby multiple species develop from a common ancestor to take advantage of diverse ecological conditions such as the California lilac (*[Ceanothus](/wiki/Ceanothus "Ceanothus")*).[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*] Many California endemics have become endangered, as urbanization, logging, [overgrazing](/wiki/Overgrazing "Overgrazing"), and the introduction of [exotic species](/wiki/Exotic_species "Exotic species") have encroached on their habitat.

### Flora and fauna

Main articles: [Fauna of California](/wiki/Fauna_of_California "Fauna of California") and [California Floristic Province](/wiki/California_Floristic_Province "California Floristic Province")

See also: [List of California native plants](/wiki/List_of_California_native_plants "List of California native plants")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Grizzly_Giant_Mariposa_Grove.jpg/250px-Grizzly_Giant_Mariposa_Grove.jpg)](/wiki/File:Grizzly_Giant_Mariposa_Grove.jpg)

Yosemite's [Grizzly Giant](/wiki/Grizzly_Giant "Grizzly Giant"), a 209' tall giant sequoia, Earth's [largest tree species](/wiki/List_of_tallest_trees "List of tallest trees").[[146]](#cite_note-148) Listed as endangered by the [IUCN](/wiki/IUCN "IUCN"), most [sequoia groves](/wiki/List_of_giant_sequoia_groves "List of giant sequoia groves") have been granted protected status.[[147]](#cite_note-149)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/JoshuaTree_20150911.jpg/250px-JoshuaTree_20150911.jpg)](/wiki/File:JoshuaTree_20150911.jpg)

Originally utilized by [Indigenous peoples](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California") as a source of food and fiber for textiles, the western Joshua Tree (*[Yucca brevifolia](/wiki/Yucca_brevifolia "Yucca brevifolia")*) is a recognizable native plant of Californian deserts and protected under the State's *Western Joshua Tree Conservation Act* of 2023.[[148]](#cite_note-150)[[149]](#cite_note-151)[[150]](#cite_note-152)

California boasts several superlatives in its collection of flora: the [largest trees](/wiki/Giant_sequoia "Giant sequoia"), the [tallest trees](/wiki/Coast_redwood "Coast redwood"), and the [oldest trees](/wiki/Pinus_longaeva "Pinus longaeva"). California's native grasses are [perennial plants](/wiki/Perennial_plant "Perennial plant"),[[151]](#cite_note-Restoring_Native_Grasses-153) and there are close to hundred succulent species native to the state.[[152]](#cite_note-154) After European contact, these were generally replaced by [invasive species](/wiki/Invasive_species "Invasive species") of European annual grasses; and, in modern times, California's hills turn a characteristic golden-brown in summer.[[145]](#cite_note-The_California_Invasive_Species_List-147)

Because California has the greatest diversity of climate and terrain, the state has six life zones which are the lower [Sonoran Desert](/wiki/Sonoran_Desert "Sonoran Desert"); upper Sonoran (foothill regions and some coastal lands), transition (coastal areas and moist northeastern counties); and the Canadian, Hudsonian, and Arctic Zones, comprising the state's highest elevations.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)

Plant life in the dry climate of the lower Sonoran zone contains a diversity of native cactus, mesquite, and paloverde. The [Joshua tree](/wiki/Yucca_brevifolia "Yucca brevifolia") is found in the Mojave Desert. Flowering plants include the dwarf desert poppy and a variety of [asters](/wiki/Aster_(genus) "Aster (genus)"). [Fremont cottonwood](/wiki/Fremont_cottonwood "Fremont cottonwood") and [valley oak](/wiki/Valley_oak "Valley oak") thrive in the Central Valley. The upper Sonoran zone includes the chaparral belt, characterized by forests of small shrubs, stunted trees, and herbaceous plants. *[Nemophila](/wiki/Nemophila "Nemophila")*, [mint](/wiki/Lamiaceae "Lamiaceae"), *[Phacelia](/wiki/Phacelia "Phacelia")*, *[Viola](/wiki/Viola_(plant) "Viola (plant)")*, and the California poppy (*[Eschscholzia californica](/wiki/Eschscholzia_californica "Eschscholzia californica")*, the state flower) also flourish in this zone, along with the lupine, more species of which occur here than anywhere else in the world.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)

The transition zone includes most of California's forests with the redwood (*[Sequoia sempervirens](/wiki/Sequoia_sempervirens "Sequoia sempervirens")*) and the "big tree" or giant sequoia (*[Sequoiadendron giganteum](/wiki/Sequoiadendron_giganteum "Sequoiadendron giganteum")*), among the oldest living things on earth (some are said to have lived at least 4,000 years). [Tanbark oak](/wiki/Tanbark_oak "Tanbark oak"), [California laurel](/wiki/California_laurel "California laurel"), [sugar pine](/wiki/Sugar_pine "Sugar pine"), [madrona](/wiki/Arbutus "Arbutus"), [broad-leaved maple](/wiki/Acer_macrophyllum "Acer macrophyllum"), and [Douglas-fir](/wiki/Douglas-fir "Douglas-fir") also grow here. Forest floors are covered with [swordfern](/wiki/Polystichum "Polystichum"), alumnroot, [barrenwort](/wiki/Barrenwort "Barrenwort"), and [trillium](/wiki/Trillium "Trillium"), and there are thickets of [huckleberry](/wiki/Huckleberry "Huckleberry"), [azalea](/wiki/Azalea "Azalea"), elder, and wild currant. Characteristic wild flowers include varieties of mariposa, [tulip](/wiki/Tulip "Tulip"), and [tiger](/wiki/Lilium_columbianum "Lilium columbianum") and [leopard](/wiki/Lilium_pardalinum "Lilium pardalinum") lilies.[[154]](#cite_note-Sequoia_sempervirens_(D._Don)_Endl.-156)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/California_sea_lion_in_La_Jolla_%2870568%29.jpg/250px-California_sea_lion_in_La_Jolla_%2870568%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:California_sea_lion_in_La_Jolla_(70568).jpg)

A [California sea lion](/wiki/California_sea_lion "California sea lion") in [La Jolla](/wiki/La_Jolla "La Jolla")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tule_Elk_-_Merced_National_Wildlife_Refuge_Bill_Leikam_12-03-2010.jpg/250px-Tule_Elk_-_Merced_National_Wildlife_Refuge_Bill_Leikam_12-03-2010.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tule_Elk_-_Merced_National_Wildlife_Refuge_Bill_Leikam_12-03-2010.jpg)

A [Tule Elk](/wiki/Tule_Elk "Tule Elk") in the [San Joaquin Valley](/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley "San Joaquin Valley")

The high elevations of the Canadian zone allow the [Jeffrey pine](/wiki/Jeffrey_pine "Jeffrey pine"), [red fir](/wiki/Red_fir "Red fir"), and [lodgepole pine](/wiki/Lodgepole_pine "Lodgepole pine") to thrive. Brushy areas are abundant with dwarf [manzanita](/wiki/Manzanita "Manzanita") and ceanothus; the unique [Sierra puffball](/wiki/Calvatia_sculpta "Calvatia sculpta") is also found here. Right below the timberline, in the Hudsonian zone, the whitebark, foxtail, and silver pines grow.
