At about 10,500 feet (3,200 m), begins the Arctic zone, a treeless region whose flora include a number of wildflowers, including [Sierra primrose](/wiki/Primula_suffrutescens "Primula suffrutescens"), [yellow columbine](/wiki/Aquilegia_flavescens "Aquilegia flavescens"), [alpine buttercup](/wiki/Ranunculus "Ranunculus"), and [alpine shooting star](/wiki/Dodecatheon_alpinum "Dodecatheon alpinum").[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)[[155]](#cite_note-Life_Zones_of_the_Central_Sierra_Nevada-157)

[Palm trees](/wiki/Palm_trees "Palm trees") are a well-known feature of California, particularly in [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California") and [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles"); many species have been imported, though the *Washington filifera* (commonly known as the *California fan palm*) is native to the state, mainly growing in the [Colorado Desert](/wiki/Colorado_Desert "Colorado Desert") oases.[[156]](#cite_note-158) Other common plants that have been introduced to the state include the [eucalyptus](/wiki/Eucalyptus "Eucalyptus"), [acacia](/wiki/Acacia "Acacia"), [pepper tree](/wiki/Schinus "Schinus"), geranium, and [Scotch broom](/wiki/Scotch_broom "Scotch broom"). The species that are federally classified as endangered are the [Contra Costa wallflower](/wiki/Erysimum_capitatum "Erysimum capitatum"), [Antioch Dunes evening primrose](/wiki/Oenothera_deltoides_subsp._howellii "Oenothera deltoides subsp. howellii"), [Solano grass](/wiki/Tuctoria_mucronata "Tuctoria mucronata"), [San Clemente Island larkspur](/wiki/Delphinium_variegatum "Delphinium variegatum"), [salt marsh bird's beak](/wiki/Cordylanthus_maritimus "Cordylanthus maritimus"), [McDonald's rock-cress](/wiki/Arabis_blepharophylla "Arabis blepharophylla"), and [Santa Barbara Island liveforever](/wiki/Dudleya_traskiae "Dudleya traskiae"). As of December 1997[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit), 85 plant species were listed as threatened or endangered.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)

In the deserts of the lower Sonoran zone, the mammals include the [jackrabbit](/wiki/Jackrabbit "Jackrabbit"), [kangaroo rat](/wiki/Kangaroo_rat "Kangaroo rat"), squirrel, and opossum. Common birds include the [owl](/wiki/Owl "Owl"), [roadrunner](/wiki/Roadrunner "Roadrunner"), [cactus wren](/wiki/Cactus_wren "Cactus wren"), and various species of hawk. The area's reptilian life include the [sidewinder viper](/wiki/Crotalus_cerastes "Crotalus cerastes"), [desert tortoise](/wiki/Desert_tortoise "Desert tortoise"), and [horned toad](/wiki/Horned_toad "Horned toad"). The upper Sonoran zone boasts mammals such as the [antelope](/wiki/Pronghorn "Pronghorn"), [brown-footed woodrat](/wiki/Dusky-footed_woodrat "Dusky-footed woodrat"), and [ring-tailed cat](/wiki/Ring-tailed_cat "Ring-tailed cat"). Birds unique to this zone are the [California thrasher](/wiki/California_thrasher "California thrasher"), [bushtit](/wiki/Psaltriparus_minimus "Psaltriparus minimus"), and [California condor](/wiki/California_condor "California condor").[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)[[157]](#cite_note-California_Condor-159)[[158]](#cite_note-CalPhotos:_Browse_Mammal_Common_Names-160)[[159]](#cite_note-Quail_Ridge_Reserve:_UC_Davis_Natural_Reserve_System-161)

In the transition zone, there are Colombian [black-tailed deer](/wiki/Black-tailed_deer "Black-tailed deer"), [black bears](/wiki/American_black_bear "American black bear"), [gray foxes](/wiki/Gray_fox "Gray fox"), [cougars](/wiki/Cougar "Cougar"), [bobcats](/wiki/Bobcat "Bobcat"), and [Roosevelt elk](/wiki/Roosevelt_elk "Roosevelt elk"). Reptiles such as the garter snakes and rattlesnakes inhabit the zone. In addition, amphibians such as the [water puppy](/wiki/Proteidae "Proteidae") and [redwood salamander](/wiki/Batrachoseps_attenuatus "Batrachoseps attenuatus") are common too. Birds such as the [kingfisher](/wiki/Kingfisher "Kingfisher"), chickadee, [towhee](/wiki/Towhee "Towhee"), and hummingbird thrive here as well.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)[[160]](#cite_note-Black-tailed_Deer_of_California-162)

The Canadian zone mammals include the [mountain weasel](/wiki/Mountain_weasel "Mountain weasel"), [snowshoe hare](/wiki/Snowshoe_hare "Snowshoe hare"), and several species of chipmunks. Conspicuous birds include the [blue-fronted jay](/wiki/Steller%27s_jay "Steller's jay"), [mountain chickadee](/wiki/Mountain_chickadee "Mountain chickadee"), [hermit thrush](/wiki/Hermit_thrush "Hermit thrush"), [American dipper](/wiki/American_dipper "American dipper"), and [Townsend's solitaire](/wiki/Townsend%27s_solitaire "Townsend's solitaire"). As one ascends into the Hudsonian zone, birds become scarcer. While the [gray-crowned rosy finch](/wiki/Gray-crowned_rosy_finch "Gray-crowned rosy finch") is the only bird native to the high Arctic region, other bird species such as [Anna's hummingbird](/wiki/Anna%27s_hummingbird "Anna's hummingbird") and [Clark's nutcracker](/wiki/Clark%27s_nutcracker "Clark's nutcracker"). Principal mammals found in this region include the Sierra coney, [white-tailed jackrabbit](/wiki/White-tailed_jackrabbit "White-tailed jackrabbit"), and the [bighorn sheep](/wiki/Bighorn_sheep "Bighorn sheep"). As of April 2003[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit), the bighorn sheep was listed as endangered by the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service. The fauna found throughout several zones are the [mule deer](/wiki/Mule_deer "Mule deer"), [coyote](/wiki/Coyote "Coyote"), [mountain lion](/wiki/Mountain_lion "Mountain lion"), [northern flicker](/wiki/Northern_flicker "Northern flicker"), and several species of hawk and sparrow.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Methuselah_Walk_USA_Ca.jpg/250px-Methuselah_Walk_USA_Ca.jpg)](/wiki/File:Methuselah_Walk_USA_Ca.jpg)

[Methuselah](/wiki/Methuselah_(pine_tree) "Methuselah (pine tree)") is the [oldest tree in the world](/wiki/List_of_oldest_trees "List of oldest trees"), found in the [Ancient Bristlecone Pine Forest](/wiki/Ancient_Bristlecone_Pine_Forest "Ancient Bristlecone Pine Forest") of [Inyo National Forest](/wiki/Inyo_National_Forest "Inyo National Forest").

Aquatic life in California thrives, from the state's mountain lakes and streams to the rocky Pacific coastline. Numerous trout species are found, among them [rainbow](/wiki/Rainbow_trout "Rainbow trout"), [golden](/wiki/Golden_trout "Golden trout"), and [cutthroat](/wiki/Cutthroat_trout "Cutthroat trout"). Migratory species of salmon are common as well. Deep-sea life forms include [sea bass](/wiki/White_seabass "White seabass"), [yellowfin tuna](/wiki/Yellowfin_tuna "Yellowfin tuna"), [barracuda](/wiki/Barracuda "Barracuda"), and several types of whale. Native to the cliffs of northern California are seals, sea lions, and many types of shorebirds, including migratory species.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155)

As of April 2003[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit), 118 California animals were on the federal endangered list; 181 plants were listed as endangered or threatened. Endangered animals include the [San Joaquin kitfox](/wiki/Vulpes_macrotis "Vulpes macrotis"), [Point Arena mountain beaver](/wiki/Aplodontia_rufa_nigra "Aplodontia rufa nigra"), [Pacific pocket mouse](/wiki/Pacific_pocket_mouse "Pacific pocket mouse"), [salt marsh harvest mouse](/wiki/Salt_marsh_harvest_mouse "Salt marsh harvest mouse"), [Morro Bay kangaroo rat](/wiki/Morro_Bay_kangaroo_rat "Morro Bay kangaroo rat") (and five other species of kangaroo rat), [Amargosa vole](/wiki/California_vole#Subspecies "California vole"), [California least tern](/wiki/California_least_tern "California least tern"), [California condor](/wiki/California_condor "California condor"), [loggerhead shrike](/wiki/Loggerhead_shrike "Loggerhead shrike"), [San Clemente sage sparrow](/wiki/Bell%27s_sparrow "Bell's sparrow"), [San Francisco garter snake](/wiki/San_Francisco_garter_snake "San Francisco garter snake"), five species of salamander, three species of chub, and two species of pupfish. Eleven butterflies are also endangered[[161]](#cite_note-163) and two that are threatened are on the federal list.[[162]](#cite_note-164)[[163]](#cite_note-165) Among threatened animals are the coastal [California gnatcatcher](/wiki/California_gnatcatcher "California gnatcatcher"), [Paiute cutthroat trout](/wiki/Paiute_cutthroat_trout "Paiute cutthroat trout"), [southern sea otter](/wiki/Sea_otter#Subspecies "Sea otter"), and [northern spotted owl](/wiki/Northern_spotted_owl "Northern spotted owl"). California has a total of 290,821 acres (1,176.91 km2) of National Wildlife Refuges.[[153]](#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-155) As of September 2010[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit), 123 California animals were listed as either endangered or threatened on the [federal list](/wiki/US_Fish_%26_Wildlife_Service "US Fish & Wildlife Service").[[164]](#cite_note-U.S._Fish_&_Wildlife_Service:_Species_Reports:_Listings_and_occurrences_for_California-166) Also, as of the same year[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit), 178 species of California plants were listed either as endangered or threatened on this federal list.[[164]](#cite_note-U.S._Fish_&_Wildlife_Service:_Species_Reports:_Listings_and_occurrences_for_California-166)

### Rivers

Main article: [List of rivers of California](/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_California "List of rivers of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/View_of_the_Bay_Area_and_the_Californian_Delta.jpg/250px-View_of_the_Bay_Area_and_the_Californian_Delta.jpg)](/wiki/File:View_of_the_Bay_Area_and_the_Californian_Delta.jpg)

[San Francisco Bay](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay "San Francisco Bay") (center left) and the [California Delta](/wiki/Sacramento%E2%80%93San_Joaquin_River_Delta "Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta") (top right)

The most prominent river system within California is formed by the Sacramento River and [San Joaquin River](/wiki/San_Joaquin_River "San Joaquin River"), which are fed mostly by snowmelt from the west slope of the Sierra Nevada, and respectively drain the north and south halves of the Central Valley. The two rivers join in the [Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta](/wiki/Sacramento%E2%80%93San_Joaquin_River_Delta "Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta"), flowing into the Pacific Ocean through [San Francisco Bay](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay "San Francisco Bay"). Many major tributaries feed into the Sacramento–San Joaquin system, including the [Pit River](/wiki/Pit_River "Pit River"), [Feather River](/wiki/Feather_River "Feather River") and [Tuolumne River](/wiki/Tuolumne_River "Tuolumne River").

The [Klamath](/wiki/Klamath_River "Klamath River") and [Trinity Rivers](/wiki/Trinity_River_(California) "Trinity River (California)") drain a large area in far northwestern California. The [Eel River](/wiki/Eel_River_(California) "Eel River (California)") and [Salinas River](/wiki/Salinas_River_(California) "Salinas River (California)") each drain portions of the California coast, north and south of San Francisco Bay, respectively. The [Mojave River](/wiki/Mojave_River "Mojave River") is the primary watercourse in the Mojave Desert, and the [Santa Ana River](/wiki/Santa_Ana_River "Santa Ana River") drains much of the [Transverse Ranges](/wiki/Transverse_Ranges "Transverse Ranges") as it bisects Southern California. The [Colorado River](/wiki/Colorado_River "Colorado River") forms the state's southeast border with Arizona.

Most of California's major rivers are dammed as part of two massive water projects: the [Central Valley Project](/wiki/Central_Valley_Project "Central Valley Project"), providing water for agriculture in the Central Valley, and the [California State Water Project](/wiki/California_State_Water_Project "California State Water Project") diverting water from Northern to Southern California. The state's coasts, rivers, and other bodies of water are regulated by the [California Coastal Commission](/wiki/California_Coastal_Commission "California Coastal Commission").

### Regions

Main article: [List of regions of California](/wiki/List_of_regions_of_California "List of regions of California")

See also: [List of places in California](/wiki/List_of_places_in_California "List of places in California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ca-regions.svg/250px-Ca-regions.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Ca-regions.svg)

Map of the [regions of California](/wiki/List_of_regions_of_California "List of regions of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Southern_California_counties_in_red_noshade.png/250px-Southern_California_counties_in_red_noshade.png)](/wiki/File:Southern_California_counties_in_red_noshade.png)

Map showing the division between [Northern California](/wiki/Northern_California "Northern California") (top white) and [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California") (bottom red)

California is traditionally separated into [Northern California](/wiki/Northern_California "Northern California") and [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California"), divided by a straight border which runs across the state, separating the northern 48 counties from the southern 10 counties. Despite the persistence of the northern-southern divide, California is more precisely divided into many regions, multiple of which stretch across the northern-southern divide.

Major divisions

* **[Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California")**

### Cities and towns

See also: [List of cities and towns in California](/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_California "List of cities and towns in California") and [List of largest California cities by population](/wiki/List_of_largest_California_cities_by_population "List of largest California cities by population")

The state has 483 [incorporated](/wiki/Municipal_corporation "Municipal corporation") cities and towns,[[165]](#cite_note-483rd_city-167) of which 461 are cities and 22 are towns. Under California law, the terms "city" and "town" are explicitly interchangeable; the name of an incorporated [municipality](/wiki/Municipality "Municipality") in the state can either be "City of (Name)" or "Town of (Name)".[[166]](#cite_note-Cal_Gov_Code_34502-168)

[Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento,_California "Sacramento, California") became California's first incorporated city on February 27, 1850.[[167]](#cite_note-Sacramento_Charter-169) [San Jose](/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California"), [San Diego](/wiki/San_Diego "San Diego"), and [Benicia](/wiki/Benicia,_California "Benicia, California") tied for California's second incorporated city, each receiving incorporation on March 27, 1850.[[168]](#cite_note-San_Jose_Inc-170)[[169]](#cite_note-History_of_San_Diego-171)[[170]](#cite_note-Benicia_Inc-172) [Mountain House](/wiki/Mountain_House,_California "Mountain House, California") became the state's most recent and 483rd incorporated municipality on July 1, 2024.[[165]](#cite_note-483rd_city-167)
The majority of these cities and towns are within one of five [metropolitan areas](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area"): the [Los Angeles Metropolitan Area](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Metropolitan_Area "Los Angeles Metropolitan Area"), the [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area"), the [Riverside-San Bernardino Area](/wiki/Riverside-San_Bernardino_Area "Riverside-San Bernardino Area"), the [San Diego metropolitan area](/wiki/San_Diego_metropolitan_area "San Diego metropolitan area"), or the [Sacramento metropolitan area](/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Sacramento metropolitan area").

## Demographics

Main article: [Demographics of California](/wiki/Demographics_of_California "Demographics of California")

### Population

Historical population

| Sources: 1790–1990, 2000, 2010, 2020, 2024[[173]](#cite_note-dof.ca.gov-175)[[174]](#cite_note-census_1790_1990-176)[[175]](#cite_note-Census2020-177)[[176]](#cite_note-178) Chart does not include indigenous population figures. Studies indicate that the Native American population in California in 1850 was close to 150,000 before declining to 15,000 by 1900.[[177]](#cite_note-americanindiantah1-179) | | | |

Presently, close to one out of every nine U.S. residents live in California.[[178]](#cite_note-PPIC-180)[[179]](#cite_note-40Mill-181) According to the [2020 U.S. census](/wiki/2020_U.S._census "2020 U.S. census"), the population of California was 39.54 million on April 1, 2020, a 6.13% increase since [2010](/wiki/2010_United_States_census "2010 United States census").[[175]](#cite_note-Census2020-177) During that decade, the state's population grew more slowly than the rest of the nation, resulting in the loss of one seat on the U.S. House of Representatives, the first loss in its entire history.[[178]](#cite_note-PPIC-180) The estimated state population in 2023 was 38.94 million.[[179]](#cite_note-40Mill-181) For well over a century (1900–2020), California experienced steady population growth. Even while the rate of growth began to slow by the 1990s, some growth continued into the first two decades of the 21st century; California added an average of around 400,000 people per year to its population during the period 1940–2020.[[180]](#cite_note-182)[[181]](#cite_note-Byler-183)[[182]](#cite_note-184) Then in 2020, the state began to experience population declines continuing every year, attributable mostly to moves out of state but also due to declining [birth rates](/wiki/Birth_rate "Birth rate"), [COVID-19 pandemic deaths](/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_deaths "COVID-19 pandemic deaths"), and less internal migration from other states to California.[[178]](#cite_note-PPIC-180)[[183]](#cite_note-185) According to the U.S. Census Bureau, between 2021 and 2022, 818,000 California residents moved out of state[[184]](#cite_note-186) with emigrants listing high cost of living, [California housing shortage](/wiki/California_housing_shortage "California housing shortage")[[185]](#cite_note-187) rise of remote work,[[186]](#cite_note-188) high taxes, and a difficult business environment as the motivation.[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*] The net loss of population in California between July 2020 and July 2023 was 433,000.[[178]](#cite_note-PPIC-180)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/California_population_density_2020.png/250px-California_population_density_2020.png)](/wiki/File:California_population_density_2020.png)

California's population density, 2020

The [Greater Los Angeles Area](/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area "Greater Los Angeles Area") is the second-largest [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area") in the U.S., while Los Angeles is the [second-largest city in the U.S.](/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population "List of United States cities by population") [Los Angeles County](/wiki/Los_Angeles_County "Los Angeles County") has held the title of most populous U.S. county for decades and it alone is more populous than 42 U.S. states.[[187]](#cite_note-LA_County_DPSS-189)[[188]](#cite_note-Baby_Slump_In_L.A._County-190) San Francisco is the most densely populated city in California and [one of the most densely populated cities in the U.S.](/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population_density "List of United States cities by population density"). Four of the [top 20 most populous cities in the U.S.](/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population "List of United States cities by population") are in California: Los Angeles (2nd), [San Diego](/wiki/San_Diego "San Diego") (8th), [San Jose](/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California") (13th), and San Francisco (17th). The [center of population](/wiki/Center_of_population "Center of population") of California is located four miles west-southwest of the city of [Shafter](/wiki/Shafter,_California "Shafter, California"), [Kern County](/wiki/Kern_County,_California "Kern County, California").[[note 3]](#cite_note-192)

As of 2020, California ranked [fourth among states by life expectancy](/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_life_expectancy "List of U.S. states and territories by life expectancy"), with a life expectancy of 79.0 years.[[190]](#cite_note-193)

Starting in 2010, for the first time since the [California Gold Rush](/wiki/California_Gold_Rush "California Gold Rush"), California-born residents made up the majority of the state's population.[[191]](#cite_note-194) Along with the rest of the U.S., California's immigration pattern has also shifted over the course of the late 2000s to early 2010s.[[192]](#cite_note-Pew_Mexican_Immigration-195) Immigration from [Latin American](/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America") countries has dropped significantly with most immigrants now coming from Asia.[[193]](#cite_note-SacBee17JAN2013-196) In total for 2011, there were 277,304 immigrants; 57% came from Asian countries versus 22% from Latin American countries.[[193]](#cite_note-SacBee17JAN2013-196) [Net immigration](/wiki/Net_immigration "Net immigration") from Mexico, previously the most common country of origin for new immigrants, has dropped to zero / less than zero since more Mexican nationals are departing for their home country than immigrating.[[192]](#cite_note-Pew_Mexican_Immigration-195)

The state's population of [undocumented immigrants](/wiki/Undocumented_immigrants "Undocumented immigrants") has been shrinking in recent years, due to increased enforcement and decreased job opportunities for lower-skilled workers.[[194]](#cite_note-197) The number of migrants arrested attempting to cross the Mexican border in the Southwest decreased from a high of 1.1 million in 2005 to 367,000 in 2011.[[195]](#cite_note-BusinessWeek-198) Despite these recent trends, [illegal](/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States "Illegal immigration to the United States") [aliens](/wiki/Alien_(law) "Alien (law)") constituted an estimated 7.3% of the state's population, the third highest percentage of any state in the [country](/wiki/Illegal_immigrant_population_of_the_United_States "Illegal immigrant population of the United States"),[[196]](#cite_note-199)[[note 4]](#cite_note-200) totaling nearly 2.6 million.[[197]](#cite_note-SDUT19042011-201) In particular, illegal immigrants tended to be concentrated in [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles_County,_California "Los Angeles County, California"), [Monterey](/wiki/Monterey_County,_California "Monterey County, California"), [San Benito](/wiki/San_Benito_County,_California "San Benito County, California"), [Imperial](/wiki/Imperial_County,_California "Imperial County, California"), and [Napa Counties](/wiki/Napa_County,_California "Napa County, California")—the latter four of which have significant agricultural industries that depend on manual labor.[[198]](#cite_note-PPIC2011II-202) More than half of illegal immigrants originate from Mexico.[[197]](#cite_note-SDUT19042011-201) The state of California and some California cities, including [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles"), [Oakland](/wiki/Oakland "Oakland"), and [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco "San Francisco"),[[199]](#cite_note-203) have adopted [sanctuary policies](/wiki/Sanctuary_city "Sanctuary city").[[200]](#cite_note-204)

According to [HUD](/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development "United States Department of Housing and Urban Development")'s 2022 [Annual Homeless Assessment Report](/wiki/Annual_Homeless_Assessment_Report_to_Congress "Annual Homeless Assessment Report to Congress"), there were an estimated 171,521 [homeless](/wiki/Homelessness "Homelessness") people [in California](/wiki/Homelessness_in_California "Homelessness in California").[[201]](#cite_note-205)[[202]](#cite_note-206)

### Race and ethnicity

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ethnicity_in_California_%282020%29.jpg/250px-Ethnicity_in_California_%282020%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ethnicity_in_California_(2020).jpg)

According to the U.S. Census Bureau, in 2022 the population self-identified as (alone or in combination): 56.5% [White](/wiki/White_Americans "White Americans") (including [Hispanic Whites](/wiki/Hispanic_White_Americans "Hispanic White Americans")),[[210]](#cite_note-215) 33.7% [non-Hispanic white](/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites "Non-Hispanic whites"),[[211]](#cite_note-216) 18.1% [Asian](/wiki/Asian_American "Asian American"),[[212]](#cite_note-217) 7.3% Black or [African American](/wiki/African_American "African American"),[[213]](#cite_note-218) 3.2% [Native American](/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States") and [Alaska Native](/wiki/Alaska_Native "Alaska Native"),[[214]](#cite_note-219) 0.9% [Native Hawaiian](/wiki/Native_Hawaiian "Native Hawaiian") or [Pacific Islander](/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American "Pacific Islander American"),[[215]](#cite_note-220) and 34.3% [some other race](/wiki/Some_Other_Race "Some Other Race").[[216]](#cite_note-221) These numbers add up to more than 100% because respondents can select multiple racial identities. 19% of Californians identified as two or more races in 2022, although excluding respondents who selected "some other race", only 5% identified as two or more races.[[217]](#cite_note-222)

By ethnicity, in 2018 the population was 60.7% non-Hispanic (of any race) and 39.3% [Hispanic or Latino](/wiki/Hispanics_and_Latinos_in_California "Hispanics and Latinos in California") (of any race). Hispanics are the largest single ethnic group in California.[[218]](#cite_note-2018CensusDemo-223) [Non-Hispanic whites](/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites "Non-Hispanic whites") constituted 36.8% of the state's population.[[218]](#cite_note-2018CensusDemo-223) *[Californios](/wiki/Californio "Californio")* are the [Hispanic](/wiki/Hispanic "Hispanic") residents native to California, who make up the [Spanish-speaking](/wiki/Spanish_language_in_California "Spanish language in California") community that has existed in California since 1542, of varying [Mexican American](/wiki/Mexican_American "Mexican American")/[Chicano](/wiki/Chicano "Chicano"), [Criollo Spaniard](/wiki/Criollo_people "Criollo people"), and Mestizo origin.[[219]](#cite_note-224) However, they make up only a small part of California's Hispanic population today, estimated at 500,000. California has the largest Mexican, [Salvadoran](/wiki/Salvadoran_Americans "Salvadoran Americans"), and [Guatemalan](/wiki/Guatemalan_Americans "Guatemalan Americans") populations in the U.S., together making up over 90% of the state's Latino population.[[220]](#cite_note-225)

According to 2022 estimates from the [American Community Survey](/wiki/American_Community_Survey "American Community Survey"), 32.4% of the population had [Mexican](/wiki/Mexican_Americans "Mexican Americans") ancestry, 6.6% had [German](/wiki/German_Americans "German Americans") ancestry, 6.1% had [English](/wiki/English_Americans "English Americans") ancestry, 5.6% had [Irish](/wiki/Irish_people "Irish people") ancestry, 4.9% had [Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_Americans "Chinese Americans") ancestry, 4.3% had [Filipino](/wiki/Filipino_Americans "Filipino Americans") ancestry, 4% had [Central American](/wiki/Central_America "Central America") ancestry (Mostly [Salvadoran](/wiki/Salvadoran_Americans "Salvadoran Americans") and [Guatemalan](/wiki/Guatemalan_Americans "Guatemalan Americans")), 3.4% had [Italian](/wiki/Italian_Americans "Italian Americans") ancestry, 2.8% listed themselves as [American](/wiki/American_ancestry "American ancestry"), and 2.5% had [Indian](/wiki/Indian_Americans "Indian Americans") ancestry.[[221]](#cite_note-226)[[222]](#cite_note-227)[[223]](#cite_note-228)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Ethnic_Origins_in_California.png/330px-Ethnic_Origins_in_California.png)](/wiki/File:Ethnic_Origins_in_California.png)

Ethnic origins in California

As of 2011[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit), 75.1% of California's population younger than age 1 were minorities, meaning they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white (white Hispanics are counted as minorities).[[224]](#cite_note-229)

In terms of total numbers, California has the largest population of White Americans in the U.S., an estimated 22,200,000 residents including people identifying as white in combination with any other race. The state has the 5th largest population of African Americans in the U.S., an estimated 2,250,000 residents. California's Asian American population is estimated at 7.1 million, constituting a third of the nation's total. California's Native American population of 504,000 is the most of any state, with 103,030 identifying as Non-Hispanic and belonging mostly to the [Indigenous peoples of California](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California").[[225]](#cite_note-230)[[226]](#cite_note-231) Most of the state's Native American population identifies as Hispanic and belongs to Indigenous Mexican or Central American ethnic groups, including 185,200 identifying as [Mexican American Indian](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Mexico "Indigenous peoples of Mexico") and 67,904 identifying as [Central American Indian](/wiki/Central_american_indians "Central american indians").[[227]](#cite_note-232)

According to estimates from 2011, California has the largest [minority population](/wiki/Majority-minority_state "Majority-minority state") in the U.S. by numbers, making up 60% of the state population.[[228]](#cite_note-CensusQuickFacts-233) Over the past 25 years, the population of [non-Hispanic whites](/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites "Non-Hispanic whites") has declined, while [Hispanic](/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American "Hispanic and Latino American") and [Asian](/wiki/Asian_American "Asian American") populations have grown. Between 1970 and 2011, non-Hispanic whites declined from 80% of the state's population to 40%, while [Hispanics](/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American "Hispanic and Latino American") grew from 32% in 2000 to 38% in 2011.[[229]](#cite_note-234) It is currently projected that Hispanics will rise to 49% of the population by 2060, primarily due to domestic births rather than immigration.[[230]](#cite_note-Economist_CA_Hispanics-235) With the decline of immigration from Latin America, Asian Americans now constitute the fastest growing racial/ethnic group in California; this growth is primarily driven by immigration from [China](/wiki/China "China"), [India](/wiki/India "India"), and the [Philippines](/wiki/Philippines "Philippines"), respectively.[[231]](#cite_note-Asians_CA-236)

The majority of California's immigrants were born in Latin America (49%) or Asia (41%). Most of California's immigrant population were born in Mexico (3.8 million), the Philippines (821,136), China (795,450), India (574,498), and Vietnam (525,455) and more than half (55%) of California's immigrants were naturalized US citizens in 2023 which has increased consistently since 1990, when only 31% of immigrants were naturalized.[[232]](#cite_note-237)

### Languages

Main article: [Languages of California](/wiki/Languages_of_California "Languages of California")

See also: [California English](/wiki/California_English "California English") and [Spanish language in California](/wiki/Spanish_language_in_California "Spanish language in California")

**Languages spoken in California by more than 100,000 persons**

| Language | Population (as of 2021[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&action=edit))[[233]](#cite_note-Language2021-238) | [%](/wiki/Percentage "Percentage") |
| --- | --- | --- |
| [English](/wiki/California_English "California English") | 20,763,638 | 56.08% |
| [Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_language_in_California "Spanish language in California") | 10,434,308 | 28.18% |

| [Tagalog](/wiki/Tagalog_language_in_the_United_States "Tagalog language in the United States") | 757,488 | 2.05% |

| [Hindi](/wiki/Hindi "Hindi") | 208,148 | 0.56% |

| [Japanese](/wiki/Japanese_American "Japanese American") | 135,992 | 0.37% |
| [French](/wiki/French_language_in_the_United_States "French language in the United States") | 126,371 | 0.34% |

[English](/wiki/California_English "California English") serves as California's [de jure](/wiki/De_jure "De jure") and [de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto") [official language](/wiki/Official_language "Official language"). According to the 2021 [American Community Survey](/wiki/American_Community_Survey "American Community Survey") conducted by the U.S. Census Bureau, 56.08% (20,763,638) of California residents age 5 and older spoke only [English](/wiki/English_language "English language") at home, while 43.92% spoke another language at home. Some 60.35% of California residents who speak a language other than English at home are able to speak English "well" or "very well", with this figure varying significantly across the different linguistic groups.[[233]](#cite_note-Language2021-238) Like most U.S. states (32 out of 50), California law enshrines English as its [official language](/wiki/Official_language "Official language"), and has done so since the passage of [Proposition 63](/wiki/1986_California_Proposition_63 "1986 California Proposition 63") by California voters in 1986. Various government agencies do, and are often required to, furnish documents in the various languages needed to reach their intended audiences.[[234]](#cite_note-239)[[235]](#cite_note-AB_800_Analysis-240)[[236]](#cite_note-Hull_English_already_official-241)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/California_Constitution_1849_title_page.jpg/250px-California_Constitution_1849_title_page.jpg)](/wiki/File:California_Constitution_1849_title_page.jpg)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Proclama_al_Pueblo_de_California_%281849%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Proclama_al_Pueblo_de_California_%281849%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Proclama_al_Pueblo_de_California_(1849)_(cropped).jpg)

The [Constitution of California](/wiki/Constitution_of_California "Constitution of California") was written in both [English](/wiki/California_English "California English") (left) and [Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_language_in_California "Spanish language in California") (right) by both American and [Californio](/wiki/Californio "Californio") delegates.

[Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_language_in_California "Spanish language in California") is the most commonly spoken language in California behind English, spoken by 28.18% (10,434,308) of the state's population in 2021.[[233]](#cite_note-Language2021-238) The Spanish language has been spoken in California since 1542 and is deeply intertwined with California's cultural landscape and history.[[237]](#cite_note-242)[[238]](#cite_note-243)[[239]](#cite_note-244) Spanish was the official administrative language of California through the Spanish and Mexican eras, until 1848. Following the U.S. [Conquest of California](/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California") and the [Treaty of Guadalupe-Hidalgo](/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe-Hidalgo "Treaty of Guadalupe-Hidalgo"), the U.S. federal government guaranteed the rights of Spanish-speaking Californians. The first [Constitution of California](/wiki/Constitution_of_California "Constitution of California") was written in both languages at the [Monterey Constitutional Convention of 1849](/wiki/California_Constitutional_Conventions "California Constitutional Conventions") and protected the rights of Spanish speakers to use their language in government proceedings and mandating that all government documents be published in both English and Spanish.[[240]](#cite_note-245)

Despite the initial recognition of Spanish by early American governments in California, the revised 1879 state constitution stripped the rights of Spanish speakers and the official status of Spanish.[[241]](#cite_note-246) The growth of the [English-only movement](/wiki/English-only_movement "English-only movement") by the mid-20th century led to the passage of [1986 California Proposition 63](/wiki/1986_California_Proposition_63 "1986 California Proposition 63"), which enshrined English as the only official language in California and ended Spanish as a language of instruction in public schools.[[242]](#cite_note-Time_Bilingual-247) [2016 California Proposition 58](/wiki/2016_California_Proposition_58 "2016 California Proposition 58") reversed the prohibition on [bilingual education](/wiki/Bilingual_education "Bilingual education"), though there are still many barriers to the proliferation of Spanish bilingual education, including a shortage of teachers and lack of funding.[[243]](#cite_note-248)[[242]](#cite_note-Time_Bilingual-247)[[244]](#cite_note-249) The [government of California](/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California") has since made efforts to promote Spanish language access and bilingual education,[[245]](#cite_note-250)[[246]](#cite_note-251) as have private educational institutions in California.[[247]](#cite_note-252) Many businesses in California promote Spanish language skills for their employees, to better serve both California's Hispanic population and the larger [Spanish-speaking world](/wiki/Hispanophone "Hispanophone").[[248]](#cite_note-253)[[249]](#cite_note-254)

California has historically been one of the most linguistically diverse areas in the world, with more than 70 indigenous languages derived from 64 root languages in six language families.[[250]](#cite_note-Native_Languages_1770-255)[[251]](#cite_note-Indian_Root_Languages_1994-256) A survey conducted between 2007 and 2009 identified 23 different indigenous languages among California farmworkers.[[252]](#cite_note-257) All of California's indigenous languages are [endangered](/wiki/Endangered_language "Endangered language"), although there are now efforts toward [language revitalization](/wiki/Language_revitalization "Language revitalization").[[note 6]](#cite_note-258) California has the highest concentration nationwide of [Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_language_in_the_United_States "Chinese language in the United States"), [Vietnamese](/wiki/Vietnamese_language_in_the_United_States "Vietnamese language in the United States") and [Punjabi](/wiki/Punjabi_American "Punjabi American") speakers.

As a result of the state's increasing diversity and migration from other areas across the country and around the globe, linguists began noticing a noteworthy set of emerging characteristics of spoken [American English](/wiki/American_English "American English") in California since the late 20th century. This variety, known as [California English](/wiki/California_English "California English"), has a [vowel shift](/wiki/Vowel_shift "Vowel shift") and several other phonological processes that are different from varieties of American English used in other regions of the U.S.[[253]](#cite_note-Bucholtz-259)

### Religion

Main article: [Religion in California](/wiki/Religion_in_California "Religion in California")

See also: [List of cathedrals in California](/wiki/List_of_cathedrals_in_California "List of cathedrals in California")

Religious self-identification, per [Public Religion Research Institute](/wiki/Public_Religion_Research_Institute "Public Religion Research Institute")'s 2021 *American Values Survey*[[254]](#cite_note-260)

1. [Catholicism](/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_the_United_States "Catholic Church in the United States") (34.0%)
2. [Protestantism](/wiki/Protestantism_in_the_United_States "Protestantism in the United States") (27.0%)
3. [Jehovah's Witness](/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses "Jehovah's Witnesses") (1.00%)
4. [Mormonism](/wiki/Mormonism "Mormonism") (1.00%)
5. [Unaffiliated](/wiki/Irreligion_in_the_United_States "Irreligion in the United States") (28.0%)
6. [Buddhism](/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_United_States "Buddhism in the United States") (2.00%)
7. [Judaism](/wiki/American_Jews "American Jews") (1.00%)
8. [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_United_States "Hinduism in the United States") (1.00%)
9. Other (5.00%)

The largest [religious denominations](/wiki/Religious_denomination "Religious denomination") by number of adherents as a percentage of California's population in 2014 were the Catholic Church with 28%, Evangelical Protestants with 20%, and Mainline Protestants with 10%. Together, all kinds of Protestants accounted for 32%. Those unaffiliated with any religion represented 27% of the population. The breakdown of other religions is 1% Muslim, 2% Hindu and 2% Buddhist.[[255]](#cite_note-pew2014-261) This is a change from 2008, when the population identified their religion with the Catholic Church with 31%; Evangelical Protestants with 18%; and Mainline Protestants with 14%. In 2008, those unaffiliated with any religion represented 21% of the population. The breakdown of other religions in 2008 was 0.5% Muslim, 1% Hindu and 2% Buddhist.[[256]](#cite_note-262) The *[American Jewish Year Book](/wiki/American_Jewish_Year_Book "American Jewish Year Book")* placed the total [Jewish](/wiki/American_Jews "American Jews") population of California at about 1,194,190 in 2006.[[257]](#cite_note-263) According to the [Association of Religion Data Archives](/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives "Association of Religion Data Archives") (ARDA) the largest denominations by adherents in 2010 were the [Catholic Church](/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") with 10,233,334; [The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints](/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_in_California "The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in California") with 763,818; and the [Southern Baptist Convention](/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention "Southern Baptist Convention") with 489,953.[[258]](#cite_note-www.thearda.com-264)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Cathedral_of_San_Carlos_Borromeo_%28cropped2%29.jpg/250px-Cathedral_of_San_Carlos_Borromeo_%28cropped2%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_San_Carlos_Borromeo_(cropped2).jpg)

The [Cathedral of San Carlos Borromeo](/wiki/Cathedral_of_San_Carlos_Borromeo_(Monterey,_California) "Cathedral of San Carlos Borromeo (Monterey, California)") in Monterey, built 1791–94, is the oldest [parish](/wiki/Parish "Parish") in California.[[259]](#cite_note-265)

California has a large Catholic population due to the large numbers of Mexicans and Central Americans living within its borders. California has twelve dioceses and two archdioceses, the [Archdiocese of Los Angeles](/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Los_Angeles "Archdiocese of Los Angeles") and the [Archdiocese of San Francisco](/wiki/Archdiocese_of_San_Francisco "Archdiocese of San Francisco"), the former being the largest archdiocese in the U.S.

A [Pew Research Center](/wiki/Pew_Research_Center "Pew Research Center") survey revealed that California is somewhat less religious than the rest of the states: 62% of Californians say they are "absolutely certain" of their belief in God, while in the nation 71% say so. The survey also revealed 48% of Californians say religion is "very important", compared to 56% nationally.[[260]](#cite_note-Helfland_2008-266)

## Culture

Main article: [Culture of California](/wiki/Culture_of_California "Culture of California")

See also: [Cuisine of California](/wiki/Cuisine_of_California "Cuisine of California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/250px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hollywood_Sign_(Zuschnitt).jpg)

The [Hollywood Sign](/wiki/Hollywood_Sign "Hollywood Sign") in [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles")

The culture of California is a [Western culture](/wiki/Western_culture "Western culture") and has its modern roots in [U.S. culture](/wiki/U.S._culture "U.S. culture"), but also, historically, many [Hispanic](/wiki/Hispanic "Hispanic") [Californio](/wiki/Californio "Californio") and [Mexican](/wiki/Culture_of_Mexico "Culture of Mexico") influences. As a border and coastal state, California culture has been greatly influenced by several large immigrant populations, especially those from Latin America and Asia.[[261]](#cite_note-World_of_Opportunity-267)

California has long been a subject of interest in the public mind and has often been promoted by its boosters as a kind of paradise. In the early 20th century, fueled by the efforts of state, the building projects during the [Great Depression](/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression") and local boosters, many Americans saw the Golden State as an ideal resort destination, sunny and dry all year round with easy access to the ocean and mountains. In the 1960s, popular music groups such as [the Beach Boys](/wiki/The_Beach_Boys "The Beach Boys") promoted the image of Californians as laid-back, tanned beach-goers.

### Media and entertainment

Further information: [Media in Los Angeles](/wiki/Media_in_Los_Angeles "Media in Los Angeles"), [Media in the San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/Media_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area "Media in the San Francisco Bay Area"), and [Music in California](/wiki/Music_in_California "Music in California")

See also: [List of amusement parks in the Americas § California](/wiki/List_of_amusement_parks_in_the_Americas#California "List of amusement parks in the Americas"), [List of newspapers in California](/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_California "List of newspapers in California"), and [List of radio stations in California](/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_California "List of radio stations in California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Walt_Disney_Studios_Alameda_Entrance.jpg/250px-Walt_Disney_Studios_Alameda_Entrance.jpg)](/wiki/File:Walt_Disney_Studios_Alameda_Entrance.jpg)

[Disney](/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company "The Walt Disney Company"), headquartered in [Burbank](/wiki/Burbank,_California "Burbank, California"), is one of the world's largest media and entertainment companies.

[Hollywood](/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles") and the rest of the Los Angeles area is a major global center for entertainment, with the [U.S. film industry](/wiki/Cinema_in_the_United_States "Cinema in the United States")'s ["Big Five" major film studios](/wiki/Major_film_studio "Major film studio") ([Columbia](/wiki/Columbia_Pictures "Columbia Pictures"), [Disney](/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures "Walt Disney Pictures"), [Paramount](/wiki/Paramount_Pictures "Paramount Pictures"), [Universal](/wiki/Universal_Pictures "Universal Pictures"), and [Warner Bros.](/wiki/Warner_Bros. "Warner Bros.")) as well as many minor film studios being based in or around the area. Many [animation](/wiki/Animation "Animation") studios are also headquartered in the state. The four major American television commercial broadcast networks ([ABC](/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company "American Broadcasting Company"), [CBS](/wiki/CBS "CBS"), [NBC](/wiki/NBC "NBC"), and [Fox](/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company "Fox Broadcasting Company")) as well as other networks all have production facilities and offices in the state. All the four major commercial broadcast networks, plus the two major Spanish-language networks ([Telemundo](/wiki/Telemundo "Telemundo") and [Univision](/wiki/Univision "Univision")) each have at least three [owned-and-operated TV stations](/wiki/Owned-and-operated_television_stations_in_the_United_States "Owned-and-operated television stations in the United States") in California, including at least one in Los Angeles and at least one in San Francisco.[[note 7]](#cite_note-268)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Googleplex_HQ_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Googleplex_HQ_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Googleplex_HQ_(cropped).jpg)

[Google](/wiki/Google "Google"), headquartered in [Mountain View](/wiki/Mountain_View,_California "Mountain View, California"), is one of the largest [technology companies](/wiki/Technology_companies "Technology companies") in the world.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/State_Fair_2014.jpg/250px-State_Fair_2014.jpg)](/wiki/File:State_Fair_2014.jpg)

The [California State Fair](/wiki/California_State_Fair "California State Fair") is held annually during the summer at [Cal Expo](/wiki/Cal_Expo "Cal Expo") in northeastern [Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento "Sacramento").

One of the oldest radio stations in the U.S. still in existence, [KCBS (AM)](/wiki/KCBS_(AM) "KCBS (AM)") in the [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/Media_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area "Media in the San Francisco Bay Area"), was founded in 1909. [Universal Music Group](/wiki/Universal_Music_Group "Universal Music Group"), one of the "[Big Four](/wiki/Music_market "Music market")" record labels, is based in [Santa Monica](/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California "Santa Monica, California"), while [Warner Records](/wiki/Warner_Records "Warner Records") is based in [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California "Los Angeles, California"). Many independent record labels, such as [Mind of a Genius Records](/wiki/Mind_of_a_Genius_Records "Mind of a Genius Records"), are also headquartered in the state. California is also the birthplace of several international music genres, including the [Bakersfield sound](/wiki/Bakersfield_sound "Bakersfield sound"), [Bay Area thrash metal](/wiki/Bay_Area_thrash_metal "Bay Area thrash metal"), [alternative rock](/wiki/Alternative_rock "Alternative rock"), [g-funk](/wiki/G-funk "G-funk"), [nu metal](/wiki/Nu_metal "Nu metal"), [glam metal](/wiki/Glam_metal "Glam metal"), [thrash metal](/wiki/Thrash_metal "Thrash metal"), [psychedelic rock](/wiki/Psychedelic_rock "Psychedelic rock"), [stoner rock](/wiki/Stoner_rock "Stoner rock"), [punk rock](/wiki/Punk_rock "Punk rock"), [hardcore punk](/wiki/Hardcore_punk "Hardcore punk"), [metalcore](/wiki/Metalcore "Metalcore"), [pop punk](/wiki/Pop_punk "Pop punk"), [surf music](/wiki/Surf_music "Surf music"), [third wave ska](/wiki/Third_wave_ska "Third wave ska"), [west coast hip hop](/wiki/West_coast_hip_hop "West coast hip hop"), [west coast jazz](/wiki/West_coast_jazz "West coast jazz"), [jazz rap](/wiki/Jazz_rap "Jazz rap"), and many other genres. Other genres such as [pop rock](/wiki/Pop_rock "Pop rock"), [indie rock](/wiki/Indie_rock "Indie rock"), [hard rock](/wiki/Hard_rock "Hard rock"), [hip hop](/wiki/Hip_hop "Hip hop"), [pop](/wiki/Pop_music "Pop music"), [rock](/wiki/Rock_music "Rock music"), [rockabilly](/wiki/Rockabilly "Rockabilly"), [country](/wiki/Country_music "Country music"), [heavy metal](/wiki/Heavy_metal_music "Heavy metal music"), [grunge](/wiki/Grunge "Grunge"), [new wave](/wiki/New_wave_music "New wave music") and [disco](/wiki/Disco "Disco") were popularized in the state. In addition, many British bands, such as [Led Zeppelin](/wiki/Led_Zeppelin "Led Zeppelin"), [Deep Purple](/wiki/Deep_Purple "Deep Purple"), [Black Sabbath](/wiki/Black_Sabbath "Black Sabbath"), and [the Rolling Stones](/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones "The Rolling Stones") settled in the state after becoming internationally famous.

As the home of [Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley"), the Bay Area is the headquarters of several prominent [internet media](/wiki/Internet_media "Internet media"), [social media](/wiki/Social_media "Social media"), and other technology companies. Three of the ["Big Five" technology companies](/wiki/Big_Tech "Big Tech") ([Apple](/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc."), [Meta](/wiki/Meta_Platforms "Meta Platforms"), and [Google](/wiki/Google "Google")) are based in the area as well as other services such as [Netflix](/wiki/Netflix "Netflix"), [Pandora Radio](/wiki/Pandora_Radio "Pandora Radio"), [Twitter](/wiki/Twitter "Twitter"), [Yahoo!](/wiki/Yahoo! "Yahoo!"), and [YouTube](/wiki/YouTube "YouTube"). Other prominent companies that are headquartered here include [HP inc.](/wiki/HP_inc. "HP inc.") and [Intel](/wiki/Intel "Intel"). [Microsoft](/wiki/Microsoft "Microsoft") and [Amazon](/wiki/Amazon_(company) "Amazon (company)") also have offices in the area.

California, particularly [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California"),[[262]](#cite_note-269) is considered the birthplace of modern [car culture](/wiki/Car_culture "Car culture").[[263]](#cite_note-270)

Several [fast food](/wiki/Fast_food "Fast food"), [fast casual](/wiki/Fast_casual_restaurant "Fast casual restaurant"), and [casual dining](/wiki/List_of_casual_dining_restaurant_chains "List of casual dining restaurant chains") chains were also founded California, including some that have since expanded internationally like [California Pizza Kitchen](/wiki/California_Pizza_Kitchen "California Pizza Kitchen"), [Denny's](/wiki/Denny%27s "Denny's"), [IHOP](/wiki/IHOP "IHOP"), [McDonald's](/wiki/McDonald%27s "McDonald's"), [Panda Express](/wiki/Panda_Express "Panda Express"), and [Taco Bell](/wiki/Taco_Bell "Taco Bell").

### Sports

Main article: [Sports in California](/wiki/Sports_in_California "Sports in California")

See also: [List of professional sports teams in California](/wiki/List_of_professional_sports_teams_in_California "List of professional sports teams in California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Pebble-Beach-CA.jpg/250px-Pebble-Beach-CA.jpg)](/wiki/File:Pebble-Beach-CA.jpg)

[Pebble Beach Golf Links](/wiki/Pebble_Beach_Golf_Links "Pebble Beach Golf Links"), one of the best ranked [golf courses](/wiki/Golf_course "Golf course") in the world

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/LBGP05.jpg/250px-LBGP05.jpg)](/wiki/File:LBGP05.jpg)

The [Grand Prix of Long Beach](/wiki/Grand_Prix_of_Long_Beach "Grand Prix of Long Beach") is the longest running major [street race](/wiki/Street_race "Street race") in North America.

California has 18 [major professional sports league](/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada "Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada") franchises, far more than any other state. The [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area") has five major league teams, while the [Greater Los Angeles Area](/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area "Greater Los Angeles Area") is home to ten. San Diego has two major league teams and Sacramento has one. The NFL [Super Bowl](/wiki/Super_Bowl "Super Bowl") has been hosted in California 12 times at five different stadiums: [Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum "Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum"), the Rose Bowl, Stanford Stadium, [Levi's Stadium](/wiki/Levi%27s_Stadium "Levi's Stadium"), and [San Diego Stadium](/wiki/San_Diego_Stadium "San Diego Stadium"). A thirteenth, [Super Bowl LVI](/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI "Super Bowl LVI"), was held at [SoFi Stadium](/wiki/SoFi_Stadium "SoFi Stadium") in [Inglewood](/wiki/Inglewood,_California "Inglewood, California") on February 13, 2022.[[264]](#cite_note-271)

California has long had many respected collegiate sports programs. California is home to the oldest college bowl game, the annual [Rose Bowl](/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game "Rose Bowl Game"), among others.

The [NFL](/wiki/National_Football_League "National Football League") has three teams in the state: the [Los Angeles Rams](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams "Los Angeles Rams"), [Los Angeles Chargers](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Chargers "Los Angeles Chargers"), and [San Francisco 49ers](/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers "San Francisco 49ers").

[MLB](/wiki/Major_League_Baseball "Major League Baseball") has four teams in the state: the [San Francisco Giants](/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants "San Francisco Giants"), [Los Angeles Dodgers](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers "Los Angeles Dodgers"), [Los Angeles Angels](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels "Los Angeles Angels"), and [San Diego Padres](/wiki/San_Diego_Padres "San Diego Padres").[[265]](#cite_note-272)

The [NBA](/wiki/National_Basketball_Association "National Basketball Association") has four teams in the state: the [Golden State Warriors](/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors "Golden State Warriors"), [Los Angeles Clippers](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers "Los Angeles Clippers"), [Los Angeles Lakers](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers "Los Angeles Lakers"), and [Sacramento Kings](/wiki/Sacramento_Kings "Sacramento Kings"). Additionally, the [WNBA](/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association "Women's National Basketball Association") also has two teams in the state: the [Los Angeles Sparks](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Sparks "Los Angeles Sparks") and [Golden State Valkyries](/wiki/Golden_State_Valkyries "Golden State Valkyries").

The [NHL](/wiki/National_Hockey_League "National Hockey League") has three teams in the state: the [Anaheim Ducks](/wiki/Anaheim_Ducks "Anaheim Ducks"), [Los Angeles Kings](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings "Los Angeles Kings"), and [San Jose Sharks](/wiki/San_Jose_Sharks "San Jose Sharks").

[MLS](/wiki/Major_League_Soccer "Major League Soccer") has four teams in the state: the [Los Angeles Galaxy](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Galaxy "Los Angeles Galaxy"), [San Jose Earthquakes](/wiki/San_Jose_Earthquakes "San Jose Earthquakes"), [Los Angeles FC](/wiki/Los_Angeles_FC "Los Angeles FC"), and [San Diego FC](/wiki/San_Diego_FC "San Diego FC").

[MLR](/wiki/Major_League_Rugby "Major League Rugby") has one team in the state: the [San Diego Legion](/wiki/San_Diego_Legion "San Diego Legion").

California is the only U.S. state to have hosted both the [Summer](/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games "Summer Olympic Games") and [Winter](/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games "Winter Olympic Games") Olympics. The [1932](/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics "1932 Summer Olympics") and [1984](/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics "1984 Summer Olympics") summer games were held in [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles"). Squaw Valley Ski Resort (now [Palisades Tahoe](/wiki/Palisades_Tahoe "Palisades Tahoe")) in the Lake Tahoe region hosted the [1960 Winter Olympics](/wiki/1960_Winter_Olympics "1960 Winter Olympics"). Los Angeles will host the [2028 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2028_Summer_Olympics "2028 Summer Olympics"), marking the fourth time that California will have hosted the Olympic Games.[[266]](#cite_note-273) Multiple games during the [1994 FIFA World Cup](/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup "1994 FIFA World Cup") took place in California, with the [Rose Bowl](/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Stadium "Rose Bowl Stadium") hosting eight matches (including the [final](/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup_Final "1994 FIFA World Cup Final")), while [Stanford Stadium](/wiki/Stanford_Stadium "Stanford Stadium") hosted six matches.

In addition to the Olympic games, California also hosts the [California State Games](/wiki/California_State_Games "California State Games").

Many sports, such as [surfing](/wiki/Surfing "Surfing"), [snowboarding](/wiki/Snowboarding "Snowboarding"), and [skateboarding](/wiki/Skateboarding "Skateboarding"), were invented in California, while others like [volleyball](/wiki/Volleyball "Volleyball"), [beach soccer](/wiki/Beach_soccer "Beach soccer"), and [skiing](/wiki/Skiing "Skiing") were popularized in the state.

Other sports that are big in the state include [golf](/wiki/Golf "Golf"), [rodeo](/wiki/Rodeo "Rodeo"), [tennis](/wiki/Tennis "Tennis"), [mountain climbing](/wiki/Mountain_climbing "Mountain climbing"), [marathon running](/wiki/Marathon "Marathon"), [horse racing](/wiki/Horse_racing "Horse racing"), [bowling](/wiki/Bowling "Bowling"), [mixed martial arts](/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts "Mixed martial arts"), [boxing](/wiki/Boxing "Boxing"), and [motorsports](/wiki/Motorsports "Motorsports"), especially [NASCAR](/wiki/NASCAR "NASCAR") and [Formula One](/wiki/Formula_One "Formula One").

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/The_%22Olympic_Gateway%22_arch_and_male_and_female_statues_at_the_entrance_to_the_Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum%2C_Los_Angeles%2C_California_LCCN2013631630.tif/lossy-page1-250px-The_%22Olympic_Gateway%22_arch_and_male_and_female_statues_at_the_entrance_to_the_Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum%2C_Los_Angeles%2C_California_LCCN2013631630.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_%22Olympic_Gateway%22_arch_and_male_and_female_statues_at_the_entrance_to_the_Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum,_Los_Angeles,_California_LCCN2013631630.tif)

[Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum](/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum "Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum") hosted the [Summer Olympics](/wiki/Summer_Olympics "Summer Olympics") in [1932](/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics "1932 Summer Olympics") and [1984](/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics "1984 Summer Olympics"), and will also host in [2028](/wiki/2028_Summer_Olympics "2028 Summer Olympics").
